Her mother is [[Brazil]]ian and her father is German."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"29638958":{"pageid":29638958,"ns":0,"title":"Alexandra Stan","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{EngvarB|date=April 2014}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=April 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Alexandra Stan\n| image           =File:Alexandra Stan in Sofia.JPG\n| caption         = Stan during a concert in [[Sofia]], [[Bulgaria]].\n| alt                 = Alexandra Stan\n| years_active    = 2009-present<br/><small>(hiatus: 2013)</small><ref>http://dance.fusion.fm/news/2013/10/alexandra-stan-taking-break/</ref>\n| background      = solo_singer\n| birth_name      = Alexandra Ioana Stan\n| birth_date      = {{birth date and age|df=yes|1989|6|10}}<ref>[http://www.allmusic.com/artist/alexandra-stan-mn0002651146 allmusic.com Alexandra Stan profile]</ref>\n| birth_place          =[[Constan\u021ba]], [[Romania]]\n| residence  = [[Constanta]] , [[Romania]]\n| label           = Media Pro, [[Ultra Records|Ultra]], [[Roton (label)|Roton Music]], Fonogram, Ego Italy, [[All Around the World Productions|AATW]], [[Victor Entertainment]]\n| instrument      = Vocals\n| genre           = [[House music|House]], [[Pop music|pop]], [[dance music|dance]], [[dubstep]], [[Electronic Music|electronic]], [[reggae fusion]]\n| occupation      = [[singer]], [[songwriter]], [[Model (person)|model]], [[dancer]]\n| associated_acts = \n| website = [http://alexandrastantheartist.com Alexandra Stan The Artist's website]\n}}\n\n'''Alexandra Stan''' (born 10 June 1989) is a [[Romania]]n [[singer]], [[songwriter]], [[Model (person)|model]] and occasional [[dancer]]. She released her debut single, \"[[Lollipop (Param Pam Pam)]]\", in late 2009, which peaked at number-eighteen in the [[Romanian Top 100]]. The song became known in her native country through the saxophone-dubb in its refrain, which was later used also in her next single, called \"[[Mr. Saxobeat]]\". It became her worldwide breakthrough hit, selling circa 10,000,000 copies in less than a year and reaching the charts' first position in nine countries, the top five in over thirty countries, such as [[New Zealand]] and the [[United Kingdom]], and the top 10 in [[Australia]], and top 30 in [[Canada]] and [[United States]]. She released her debut album in August 2011, titled ''[[Saxobeats]]'', which sold in over four million shipments worldwide. The album spawned two more singles: \"[[Get Back (ASAP)|Get Back]]\" and \"[[1.000.000 (song)|1,000,000]]\", featuring rapper [[Carlprit]]. The records were top-forty successes in more [[Europe]]an countries like [[Italy]] or [[Bulgaria]].\n\nStan released \"[[Lemonade (Alexandra Stan song)|Lemonade]]\" as the lead single from the Japanese re-release of her debut album ''Saxobeats''. The song charted majorly and was certified Gold in [[Italy]] by the [[Federation of the Italian Music Industry]]. She then released \"[[Cliche (Hush Hush)]]\" as the follow-up to \"[[Lemonade (Alexandra Stan song)|Lemonade]]\" on 27 September 2012, and as the second single from the re-released album. The single failed to achieve the success of its predecessor. A collaboration with Manilla Maniacs for the song \"[[All My People]]\" was selected as the third and final single from the record. The song was released on 1 May 2013, with the latter two singles both receiving moderate success.\n\nStan's second studio album was released on August 27, 2014 exclusively in [[Japan]], under the label [[Victor Entertainment]]. ''[[Dance (Alexandra Stan song)|Dance]]'' and ''[[Cherry Pop]]'' are the record's lead singles. They became populary, when they both reached the first position in the [[Japan]]ese iTunes Chart. Stan revealed the international release of her album, \"[[Unlocked (Alexandra Stan album)|Unlocked]]\", on Facebook, already weeks before its worldwide release.<ref>[https://www.facebook.com/AlexandraStanTheArtist]</ref> The album was released internationally on November 25, 2014 and it features a collaboration with [[Connect-R]] to the song ''[[Vanilla Chocolat]]''. The record sold in over 3.000 shipments in its first days after the release.\n\nStan has been reported to have a net worth of 20,000,000 \u20ac. She is also currently one of the wealthiest musical artists in [[Romania]] and [[Eastern Europe]].<ref>http://www.radio21.ro/muzica/stiri-din-muzica/alexandra-stan-in-topul-incasarilor-credidam</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4412606":{"pageid":4412606,"ns":0,"title":"Alison Limerick","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Alison Limerick\n|image = \n|caption = \n|image_size = \n|background = solo_singer\n|birth_name = Alison T. Though\u2013 Armin is No. 1 again!|url=http://www.armadamusic.com/news/2012/10/17-armada-djs-in-dj-mag-top-100-armin-is-1-again/|accessdate=19 October 2012}}</ref> He is currently ranked World No. 3 on DJ Magazine's list for 2014. Their lineup currently consists of Robbie Chater on keyboards and Tony Di Blasi on keyboards, bass, and backing vocals.<ref name=\"hsun\" />\n\nThe Avalanches' only full-length album, ''Since I Left You'', was a critical and commercial success, peaking in the top&nbsp;10 on the [[UK&nbsp;Albums Chart]] in April&nbsp;2001. At the [[ARIA Music Awards of 2001]], the group received nine nominations and won four categories, including \"Best New Artist \u2013 Album\". In October&nbsp;2010, the album was listed at No.&nbsp;10 in the book, ''[[100&nbsp;Best Australian Albums]]''. It has also been named #1&nbsp;Australian Album of all time in a Triple&nbsp;J industry poll, as well as the #10 album of the decade by [[Pitchfork Media]]. It is estimated that in the decade since its release the album has gone on to sell over a million copies.\n\nSince the release of ''Since I Left You'', the Avalanches have played several live DJ sets while also undergoing major lineup changes. Rumors of a second album have been strong since the mid-2000s. In the next year's [[Triple J Hottest 100, 2010|list]], \"Way Back Home\", reached No. 46."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2193882":{"pageid":2193882,"ns":0,"title":"Barbara Tucker","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{about||the Australian born peace activist|Barbara Grace Tucker|the African American church vocalist from Texas|Barbara Johnson Tucker}}\n{{BLP sources|date=February 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- For individuals; see Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Barbara Tucker\n| image                 = \n| alt             = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = Barbara Tucker\n| alias               = \n| death_date                = \n| origin              = [[Brooklyn]], [[New York City|New York]]\n| instrument          = \n| genre               = [[House music|House]], [[Soul music|soul]]\n| occupation          = \n| years_active        = 1985\u2013present\n| label               = Defected Records & Positiva\n| associated_acts     = \n| website                 = \n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n\n'''Barbara Tucker''' ([[Brooklyn]], [[New York City|New York]]) is an [[African American]] [[House music|house]] and [[Soul music|soul]] [[singing|singer]], [[songwriter]] and [[choreographer]]. Her music has had an impact on mainstream and dance music across the United States and throughout Europe. Tucker had six #1 hits on the US Hot Dance Club Songs chart in the 1990s and into the 2000s, and several hits on the UK scene.<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\"/>\n\nRaised in Brooklyn, New York, Barbara started singing through her entertainer father, Jayotis Washington of the group, The Persuasions. As an actress, Barbara has performed in various off-Broadway plays which allowed her to receive the \"T.O.R.\" award through the American Theater for actors for 'most promising actress with distinguishing artiste'.  As a dancer, she has choreographed and danced for various dance artist such as C&C Music Factory, Soul System, Jay Williams, and Dee-Lite. She also choreographed the first Club Music Award show and is choreographer for the Underground Network dancers. She has been managed by celebrity and sports manager [[Glenn Toby]].\n\nAs a vocalist, Barbara has recorded with and sang background vocals for such esteemed artists as [[Deee-Lite]] and [[George Clinton (musician)|George Clinton]]. She's had many underground tunes such as 'Set It Off', 'Black Delilah Dee', 'Open Your Heart' and she was featured on 'Unity'. In her ongoing career as a singer of soulful house, she has collaborated with such house music producers as David Guetta and Blaze. She is signed to the production team Masters At Work (Little Louie Vega & Kenny \"Dope\" Gonzalez) which brought forth such tunes as \"Deep Inside\", \"Beautiful People\", \"I Get Lifted\", \"Stay Together\" and \"Stop Playing With My Mind\".\n\nTucker has also become the only recording artist to boast a yearly residency at Europe\u2019s clubbing mecca, Ibiza.{{citation needed|date=July 2014}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"14423354":{"pageid":14423354,"ns":0,"title":"The Basement Boys","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"'''The Basement Boys''' is an [[United States|American]] [[House music|house-music]] [[record producer|production]] team that was formed in [[Baltimore, Maryland|Baltimore]], [[Maryland]]. The founding members, Jay Steinhour, Teddy Douglas, and Thommy Davis, all of whom had experience as [[deejay]]s in the [[Mid-Atlantic states]], began producing together in 1986.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/basement-boys-biography/|title=The Basement Boys Biography|publisher=[[IMO Records]]|accessdate=25 January 2012}}</ref> In 1988, the group scored a [[hit single]] together with \"Love Don't Live Here Anymore,\" which hit #25 on the U.S. [[Hot Dance Club Songs|Dance Club Play]] and #31 on the [[Hot Dance Singles Sales|Maxi-Singles]]  charts.<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p54778|pure_url=yes}} Billboard Singles], Allmusic.com</ref> In 1989, Davis left the group and DJ Spen joined. Karizma was also a member of the group during the mid-to-late 1990s.\n\nThe group would go on to [[remix]] or produce artists such as [[Paula Abdul]], [[Michael Jackson]], [[Erykah Badu]], [[Bob Sinclar]], [[Crystal Waters]], and [[Ultra Nat\u00e9]], and began its own [[record label]], Basement Boys Records, in 1994.<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p54778|pure_url=yes}} Biography], Allmusic.com</ref> In 2006, the group released an [[album]] titled ''The Basement Boys Present Mudfoot Jones'', which was a collection of [[remix]]es of songs by a fictional [[drummer]].\n\nThe group's only chart entry in the [[UK Singles Chart]] occurred in February 1991, presenting Ultra Nat\u00e9, on \"Is It Love?\" (UK #71).<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 44}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"347264":{"pageid":347264,"ns":0,"title":"Basement Jaxx","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=May 2014}}\n{{EngvarB|date=May 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Basement Jaxx\n| image           = Basement Jaxx.jpg\n| caption         = Basement Jaxx in 2009. Their debut single, \"[[How to Dance]]\", featuring [[Princessa (singer)|Princessa]], hit #1 on the dance chart and climbed to #25 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. It contained samples from \"[[Dance, Dance, Dance (Yowsah, Yowsah, Yowsah)]]\" by [[Chic (band)|Chic]], \"[[Dance (Disco Heat)]]\" by [[Sylvester James|Sylvester]], \"[[Kiss (Prince song)#Art of Noise feat. Tom Jones version|Kiss]]\" by [[Art of Noise]] featuring [[Tom Jones (singer)|Tom Jones]], the popular [[James Brown]] \"[[Yeah! Woo!]]\" sample loop, the bassline [[Motif (music)|motif]] from [[Mantronix]]'s single \"[[Got to Have Your Love]]\", a [[synth]] motif from [[The Whispers]]' \"[[And the Beat Goes On (The Whispers song)|And the Beat Goes On]]\", and spoken male dialogue from a K-Tel [[disco]] instructional album released in the 1970s.\n\nA follow-up single, a cover of [[The SOS Band]]'s song \"Borrowed Love,\" hit #32 on the dance chart and #71 on the Hot 100 later in the year.  Princessa rapped on that track while featured vocals were performed by Arnold Jarvis. That same year, Bingoboys remixed three songs by [[Falco (musician)|Falco]] (\"[[Der Kommissar (song)|Der Kommissar]]\", \"Junge Roemer\" and \"Wiener Blut\") for Falco's album, ''The Remix Hit Thom Jongkind, then operating as Scalix decided to set up a DJ duo with another producer at the time. The project was called Blasterjaxx. When it folded, Thom continued with the Blasterjaxx label himself. Jongkind had a few collaborations with Idir Makhlaf, then operating under the name Macosta. Makhlaf eventually joined Blasterjaxx and in 2012, the ''Reborn EP'' was released with D-Rashid  containing two tracks: \"Reborn\" and \"Where We Go\" with Laidback Luke signing the tracks at his own label Mixmash Records. Early 2013, they produced ''Loud & Proud'' together with Billy The Kit, with Ti\u00ebsto signing the track at his own record label Musical Freedom. Blasterjaxx remixed Ti\u00ebsto's hits \"Adagio for Strings\" and \"Love Comes Again\" and a collaboration on the remix of \"United\", the official anthem of Ultra Music Festival. They [[record chart|charted]] two [[song]]s on the [[United States|US]] ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]].\n\n\"[[Naked In The Rain]]\" was a #4 hit in the [[UK Singles Chart]] and a #5 dance hit in the US in 1990, which was originally issued on blue [[gramophone record|vinyl]].  It was followed by \"(Can You) Feel the Passion\" (whose melody samples [[Bizarre Inc]]'s \"Playing With Knives\"), which hit #1 on both Billboard's Dance Club Play and the [[UK Dance Chart]] in 1992, reaching #14 on the UK Singles Chart. They also had a minor hit in the [[UK Singles Chart]] in November 1990 with the #31 hit, \"Little Brother\".<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| It was formed by the two [[Disc jockey|DJ]]s Mark J Klak and Mirko Jacob.\n\nTheir collaboration started in 2000, when Mirko Jacob started performing in Klak's JoueJoueClub in [[Erfurt]]. Jacob has since left the group, and his place was filled by [[Australia]]n-born Jon Henderson.\n\nIn Autumn 2003, Boogie Pimps released their first [[Single (music)|single]], a remix of [[Jefferson Airplane]] [[cover version|cover]] of [[The Great Society (band)|The Great Society]]'s \"[[Somebody to Love (Jefferson Airplane song)|Somebody to Love]]\". In January 2004, this song entered the Top Ten of the [[UK Singles Chart]].<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 71}}</ref> The [[music video]] for \"Somebody to Love\" was an instant [[Chart-topper|hit]] in the [[United Kingdom|UK]]. It features several infants [[sky diving]] out of an [[aeroplane]] towards a giant woman ([[Natasha Mealey]]) lying on a grassy hill country landscape in her underwear, singing the song.\n\nTheir second single, \"[[Sunny (song)|Sunny]]\" was also a [[cover song]]. It was originally recorded by [[Bobby Hebb]] but the version was [[cover version|covered]] by [[Candee Jay]].\n\nIn 2004 they appeared on a [[white label]], which was not widely released, under the [[pseudonym]] 'Pimps Guerilla'. They performed songs such as \"Right Out of Here\" and \"Make 'em Drop\". While \"Make 'em Drop\" made it onto a few [[compilation album|compilations]], \"Right Out of Here\" is not commercially available, with the exception of whitelabels. This could be for legal reasons, as extracts of lyrics and melody were sampled from the end of [[Queen (band)|Queen]]'s \"[[Bohemian Rhapsody]]\".{{Citation needed|date=October 2007}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"7789430":{"pageid":7789430,"ns":0,"title":"Booka Shade","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{refimprove|date=January 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist \n|name = Booka Shade\n|image = Booka.jpg\n|caption = Booka Shade at [[Detroit Electronic Music Festival|DEMF]] in 2007\n|background = group_or_band\n|origin = [[Frankfurt]], [[Germany]]\n|Instruments =\n|genre = [[House music|House]], [[tech house]], [[minimal techno|minimal]]\n|Formed = [[2004]]\n|years_active = \n|label = [[Get Physical Records]] (2002-present)\n|website = [http://www.bookashade.com/ www.BookaShade.com]\n|current_members = [http://www.discogs.com/artist/Walter+Merziger Walter Merziger]<br/>[http://www.discogs.com/artist/Arno+Kammermeier Arno Kammermeier]\n|past_members = \n}}\n\n'''Booka Shade''' is a [[Germany|German]] [[House music|house]] duo. Boris is usually known for [[house music|funky/deep house]] tracks, mostly produced in conjunction with [[Mousse T.]] and Michi Lange, his partners in the Peppermint Jam Records label.\n\nBoris Dlugosch started his career as a DJ in the German night club Front.  Dlugosch differed from his countrymen by playing house music tracks, instead of [[happy hardcore]] or [[trance music|trance]], more established in Germany. As a producer, however, Dlugosch's first works, in the early 1990s, were in the happy hardcore genre, working alongside Gary D.\n\nDlugosch had a few occasional hits in the club circuit in the 1990s, beginning with the two tracks created with Mousse T. under the Booom! moniker, \"Hold Your Head Up High\" and \"Keep Pushin'\", with vocals by [[Inaya Day]], and \"Check It Out (Everybody)\", under the [[pseudonym|alias]] BMR (a regular partnership with Michi Lange).  More recently, Dlugosch's name achieved some fame in the year 1999 thanks to his remix of [[Moloko]]'s \"[[Sing It Back]]\", which became a club music phenomenon.  He followed up under his own name with \"Never Enough\", a track that featured the voice of Moloko's vocalist [[R\u00f3is\u00edn Murphy]]. It peaked at #16 in the [[UK Singles Chart]] in June 2001.<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 161}}</ref>\n\nBoris Dlugosch has also [[remix]]ed dozens of songs, including [[Mariah Carey]], [[Mary J. Blige]], Italian [[rapping|rapper]] [[Jovanotti]], disco band [[First Choice (music group)|First Choice]], and other well-known electronic music artists such as [[A-ha]], [[R\u00f6yksopp]], [[Moloko]] and [[Daft Punk]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"5280963":{"pageid":5280963,"ns":0,"title":"Brad Carter","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Steriogram]] {{R from merge}} This redirects to the Guitarist.\n\n{{DEFAULTSORT:Carter, Brad}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"25292690":{"pageid":25292690,"ns":0,"title":"Brian Butler","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{for|the art dealer|Brian D. {{flatlist|\n* [[Tori Amos]]\n* [[Paul van Dyk]]\n* [[Jan Johnston]]\n* [[Kirsty Hawkshaw]]\n* [[Billie Ray Martin]]\n* [[Ti\u00ebsto]]\n* [[Armin van Buuren]]\n* [[Jes Brieden|JES]]\n* [[Christian {{URL|http://www.btmusic.com/|BTMusic.com}}\n}}\n'''Brian Wayne Transeau''' (born October 4, 1970), better known by his stage name '''BT''', is an American [[Record producer|music producer]], [[composer]], technologist, [[Audio engineering|audio technician]], [[multi-instrumentalist]], [[singer]], and [[songwriter]]. An artist in the [[electronica]] music genre, he is credited as a pioneer of the [[Trance music|trance]] and [[intelligent dance music]] styles that paved the way for [[Electronic dance music|EDM]],<ref name=\"tgray\">Tyler Gray, [http://www.fastcompany.com/3019084/reverse-engineered/would-you-want-to-hear-this-new-circa-news-sound-whenever-news-breaks \u201cWould You Want to Hear This New Circa News Sound Whenever News Breaks?\u201d] ''[[Fast Company (magazine)|Fast Company]]'', October 3, 2013.</ref> and for \"stretching electronic music to its technical breaking point.\"<ref>Curtis Silver, [http://www.wired.com/2010/02/bt-these-hopeful-machines/ \u201cBT Talks These Hopeful Machines, Math and Inspiration,\u201d] ''[[Wired (magazine)|Wired]]'', February 2, 2010.</ref> He also creates music within many other styles, such as classical, film composition and bass music.\n\nBT is also known for pioneering the [[stutter edit]].<ref name=\"cperry\">Clayton Perry, [http://www.seattlepi.com/lifestyle/blogcritics/article/Interview-Brian-Transeau-Singer-Songwriter-886997.php \u201cInterview: Brian Transeau \u2013 Singer, Songwriter and Producer,\u201d] ''[[Seattle Post-Intelligencer]]'', April 26, 2011.</ref> This production technique consists of taking a small fragment of sound and repeating it rhythmically.<ref name=\"clukacs\">Cosmin Lukacs, [http://www.trancesound.net/2010/09/10/interview-with-bt-aka-brian-transeau/ \u201cInterview With BT aka Brian Transeau,\u201d] Trance Sound, September 10, 2010.</ref> BT was entered into the ''[[Guinness Book of World Records]]'' for his song \"[[Somnambulist (Simply Being Loved)]]\", recognized as using the largest number of vocal edits in a song (6,178 edits).<ref name=\"tgray\"/><ref name=\"cperry\"/><ref name=\"rslomowicz\">DJ Ron Slomowicz, [http://dancemusic.about.com/cs/features/a/Ron2k3Pick.htm \u201c21 Records That Made Me Happy to Be a DJ,\u201d] [[About.com]]. Accessed August 3, 2014.</ref> BT's work with stutter edit techniques led to the formation of software development company Sonik Architects, developer of the sound-processing software plug-ins Stutter Edit and BreakTweaker, and the live audio and visual remix app called Sonifi.<ref name=\"clukacs\"/>\n\nIn 2010, BT was nominated for a [[Grammy Award for Best Electronic/Dance Album]] for ''[[These Hopeful Machines]]''.<ref name=\"btgrammy1\">BT, [http://www.grammy.com/blogs/first-time-nominee-bt-part-one \u201cFirst-Time Nominee: BT (Part One),\u201d] [[Grammy.com]], January 18, 2011.</ref> He has produced, remixed, written for and collaborated with a variety of artists, including [[Paul van Dyk]], [[Peter Gabriel]], [[Tori Amos]], [[Depeche Mode]], [[NSYNC]], [[Sting (musician)|Sting]], [[Blake Lewis]], [[The Roots]], [[Guru (rapper)|Guru]], [[Madonna (entertainer)|Madonna]], [[Britney Spears]] and [[Ti\u00ebsto]], and composed original scores for films such as ''[[Go (1999 film)|Go]]'', ''[[The Fast and the Furious (2001 film)|The Fast and the Furious]]'' and ''[[Monster (2003 film)|Monster]]''.<ref name=\"tgray\"/><ref>David Battino, Kelli Richards, ''The Art Of Digital Music'', Backbeat Books, 2005, p. 10</ref><ref name=\"dfonooni\">Damon Fonooni, [http://www.lunarmagazine.com/features/bt.php \u201cEmbracing BT,\u201d] ''Lunar'', 2002.</ref><ref name=\"sevans\">Steph Evans, [http://www.earmilk.com/2013/08/20/earmilk-interview-bt/ \u201cEarmilk Interview: BT,\u201d] Earmilk, August 20, 2013.</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"25382731":{"pageid":25382731,"ns":0,"title":"The Buffalo Bunch","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2014}}\n'''The Buffalo Bunch''' is a [[French house]] [[Musical ensemble|duo]] consisting of musicians Paul de Homem-Christo (Play Paul; brother of [[Guy-Manuel de Homem-Christo]]) and Romain S\u00e9o. Calvin Harris works as a freelance record producer, therefore he is not associated to anyone or artists.-->\n| website         = {{URL|www.calvinharris.co.uk}}\n}}\n\n'''Adam Richard Wiles''' (born 17 January 1984), better known by his stage name '''Calvin Harris''', is a Scottish singer, songwriter, record producer and DJ. His [[British Phonographic Industry#Sales certificates|gold-selling]] debut album, ''[[I Created Disco]]'', was released in 2007 and contained the top-ten singles \"[[Acceptable in the 80s]]\" and \"[[The Girls (song)|The Girls]]\". His second studio album, ''[[Ready for the Weekend (album)|Ready for the Weekend]]'' (2009), reached number one on the [[UK Albums Chart]] and includes \"[[I'm Not Alone (song)|I'm Not Alone]]\", which debuted at number one on the [[UK Singles Chart]], the top-five hit \"[[Ready for the Weekend (song)|Ready for the Weekend]]\", and the singles \"[[Flashback (Calvin Harris song)|Flashback]]\" and \"[[You Used to Hold Me (Calvin Harris song)|You Used to Hold Me]]\".\n\nIn October 2012, Harris released his third studio album, ''[[18 Months]]'', which contained the singles, \"[[Bounce (Calvin Harris song)|Bounce]]\", \"[[Feel So Close]]\", \"[[Let's Go (Calvin Harris song)|Let's Go]]\", \"[[We'll Be Coming Back]]\", \"[[Sweet Nothing (Calvin Harris song)|Sweet Nothing]]\", \"[[Drinking from the Bottle]]\", \"[[I Need Your Love (Calvin Harris song)|I Need Your Love]]\", and \"[[Thinking About You (Calvin Harris song)|Thinking About You]]\". All of these singles reached the UK top 10. Harris has also written and produced tracks for other recording artists, including [[Kylie Minogue]], [[Sophie Ellis-Bextor]], [[Dizzee Rascal]], [[Cheryl Cole]], [[Rita Ora]], [[Example (musician)|Example]], and [[Rihanna]]'s internationally successful single, \"[[We Found Love]]\", which gave him his first US number-one single on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. The duo started out as an independent group, during their years at [[Berkeley High School (Berkeley, California)|Berkeley High School]]. The two were first signed to the label Indie-Pop. Singer-Vine left the group in August 2012 with Hollowell-Dhar continuing on with the name The Cataracs despite David's departure. She was born in [[Chicago]], [[Illinois]].  She began having [[hit record|hits]] on the [[United States|U.S.]] [[Hot Dance Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]] in the late 1990s, beginning with \"Music Is the Answer (Dancin' & Prancin'),\" a collaboration with [[disc jockey|DJ]] and [[record producer|producer]] [[Danny Tenaglia]] that peaked at number 15 in 1998. The track reached #36 in the [[UK Singles Chart]] in September 1998.<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 98}}</ref>\n\nIn 1999, Celeda released a full-length album entitled ''This Is It'' on [[Twisted Records (U.S.)|Twisted Records]] and on the [[Portugal|Portuguese]] Kaos Records. The album featured tracks produced by [[E-Smoove]], [[Danny Tenaglia]], [[Cevin Fisher]], [[Peter Rauhofer]] and [[Maurice Joshua]] among others. The tracks released as singles were \"Messin' with My Mind\" (1997), \"Music Is the Answer (Dancin' & Prancin')\" (1998), \"Be Yourself (And No One Else)\" and \"Burnin' Up\" (1999). The album also contained the dance hits \"Let the Music Use You Up\" and \"Happy\".\n\n;''This Is It'' track listing\n#\"Burnin' Up\" \n#\"Try Again\"\n#\"Hooked on You\"\n#\"Music Is the Answer (Dancin' & Prancin')\"\n#\"Happy\"\n#\"Movin' On\"\n#\"Let the Music Use You Up\"\n#\"I'm Grateful\"\n#\"Release the Power\"\n#\"Beat Me Down\"\n#\"Messin' with My Mind\"\n#\"Be Yourself (And No One Else)\" (Parts 1 & 2)\n#\"Get It Together\"\n#\"This Is It\"\n\nSince then Celeda placed four consecutive [[Single (music)|singles]] in the [[Top 40|top 10]], including \"The Underground\", which hit number one on the U.S. dance chart in 2001 (originally produced by [[Peter Rauhofer]] and remixed by [[Saeed & Palash]]).<ref>{{cite book |title= Hot Dance/Disco: 1974-2003|last=Whitburn |first=Joel |authorlink=Joel Whitburn |year=2004 |publisher=Record Research |page=53}}</ref> \"Dirtyfilthy\", a collaboration with [[Tom Stephan|Superchumbo]], became her second chart-topper in 2004, and \"Amazing\" topped the dance chart in 2008."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"25067625":{"pageid":25067625,"ns":0,"title":"Charles Schillings","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Charles Schillings\n| image = \n|caption = \n|background =  non_performing_personnel\n|origin = [[Belgium]]\n|genre = [[House music|house]]\n|years_active = \n|label = [[Pschent Music]]\n|website = [http://www.myspace.com/charlesschillings MySpace]\n| current_members = \n}}\n\n'''Charles Schillings''' is a [[French people|French]] [[House (music)|House]] [[Disc Jockey|DJ]], originally from Belgium. Fortier's DJ-ing covers a range of styles from dark progressive to minimalist techno.  He is well known for being a central figure in the development of [[electronic dance music]] in the United States as both a DJ and founder of the Balance Record Pool.<ref name=\"tranz-market\">{{cite web|url=http://www.tranzfusion.com/articles/shownews.asp?newsid=582 |title=Chris Fortier: America\u2019s Dance Market Is Huge and Growing |accessdate=2007-06-21 |date=2001-10-19 |last = Adderley |first=Jonty |author2=Angie Ng |work=Tranzfusion}}</ref>\n\nChris Fortier grew up in [[Melbourne, Florida]], moving to [[Orlando, Florida]] to attend the [[University of Central Florida]].<ref Blues |date=2004-07-18 |last=Skrufff |first=Jonty|accessdate=2007-06-21 |work=Tranzfusion}}</ref>  He began DJ-ing in 1990 in Orlando where he was influenced by other Florida DJs such as [[Kimball =http://www.jivemagazine.com/article.php?pid=3535 |title=Chris Fortier: Much More Than \"Progressive\" |date=2005-07-26 |accessdate=2007-06-20 |work=[[JIVE Magazine]]}}</ref>  In 1993, Fortier was introduced to Neil Kolo, who had been producing music for 5 years.<ref name=\"365mag-interview\">{{cite web|url=http://www.365mag.com/index.php?pg=spec&recnum=10&Title=365+Interview%3A+Chris+Fortier+on+365MAG+International+Music+Magazine |title = 365 Interview: Chris Fortier |date=2001-04-01 |accessdate=2007-06-20 |last = Blum |first = Justin |work=[[365mag]]}}</ref>  They found they had chemistry and became the duo Fade, releasing \"...For All the People\" on their newly founded label Fade Records in 1994.<ref name=\"365mag-interview\"/>  In 1996, Fortier founded the Balance Record Pool, a [[record pool]] designed to help North American DJs to spread electronic music.<ref name=\"balancepool\">{{cite web|url=http://www.balancerecordpool.com/ |publisher=Balance Record Pool |accessdate=2007-06-20 |title=Balance Record Pool}}</ref>  Balance won the [[International Dance M]]'s DJ booking agency making up Balance Promote Group.<ref name=\"365mag-interview\"/>\n\nIn 1998, when submitting a bootleg remix of [[Sarah McLachlan]]'s song \"Plenty\" to her record label, Fortier was offered the chance to remix the [[Delerium]] song \"[[Silence (song)|Silence]]\" featuring McLachlan.<ref name=\"tranz-bio\">{{cite web|url=http://www.tranzfusion.com/profiles/showprofile.asp?id=432 |title =Chris Fortier Artist Profile |accessdate=2007-06-21 |work=Tranzfusion}}</ref>  Their remix was released on [[Nettwerk]] and sold over one million copies.<ref name=\"jive-much\"/>  Fade Records began to expand to productions not exclusively by Fortier and Kolo, including helping launch the career of [[Steve Porter (producer)|Steve Porter]].<ref name=\"jive-much\"/>  Fortier helped Porter develop his production abilities and Porter helped introduce Fortier to the mixing software [[Pro Tools]].<ref The group's first short unofficial albums were released online in 2001, spreading its music through words of \"[[netizen]]s,\" who positively received the group's music. They remained underground until the release of their first album ''Instant Pig'' in 2004, selling over 80,000 copies{{Citation needed|date=October 2007}}. Since then, their music has been used in various television commercials, shows, and films, and they have been given the chance to perform at various events.<ref name=\"tjh\">Tak, Jin-Hyun. [http://news.naver.com/news/read.php?mode=LSD&office_id=073&article_id=0000021224&section_id=106&menu_id=106 Clazziquai, a new Hallyu Star] \"Sportainment\", March 4, 2006.</ref>\n\nClazziquai is known for their songs, \"Be My Love\" and \"She Is\", which were featured on the [[Korean drama]] ''[[My Lovely Samsoon]]'', with the former becoming the show's theme song. The group won an award at the MNET KM Music Video Festival for \"Best Soundtrack\", and has also been the most nominated group at the Korean Popular Music Awards II(2\ud68c), winning \"Artist of the Year\" and \"Best Pop\". The group consists of Jack Patterson, Luke Patterson, Grace Chatto, and Neil Amin-Smith.<ref name=\"4music\">{{cite episode|title=This Week's Fresh Music Top 20|publisher=[[4Music]]|airdate=15 April 2014}}</ref>\n\nTheir 2010 single \"[[Mozart's House]]\", released on [[Black Butter Records]], reached number 17 on the [[UK Singles Chart]]. In January 2014, they scored their first [[UK Singles Chart]]-topping single with \"[[Rather Be (Clean Bandit song)|Rather Be]]\", a collaboration with [[Jess Glynne]], featuring elements of both [[classical music|classical]] and [[dance music]]. \"Rather Be\" remained at the top of the chart for four weeks. In 2014, they achieved their first US Top 10 single with \"Rather Be\" peaking at number 10 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]].<ref>{{cite 2013) was a [[disc jockey]] (DJ), [[remixer]] and [[record producer|producer]] who formerly went under the moniker '''Club 69''' as well as '''Size Queen'''. After writing and recording the band's debut album ''[[While the City Sleeps, We Rule the Streets]]'' as a solo project, Saporta enlisted guitarist [[Ryland Blackinton]], bassist [[Alex Suarez]], drummer [[Nate Novarro]], and keytarist [[Victoria Asher]], all of whom provide [[Backing vocalist|backing vocals]].\n\nOn the 21st of October, 2014, Suarez and Blackinton left the band to \"start a new chapter in [their] lives in production and songwriting\".<ref name=\"Cobra Starship Blog\">{{cite web|url=http://cobrastarship.com/post/100609859130/a-farewell-from-ryland-and-alex|title=A farewell from Ryland and Alex|last=Suarez, Blackinton|first=Alex, Ryland|date=2014-10-21|work=Cobra Starship|publisher=Tumblr.com|accessdate=2014-10-22}}</ref> The band formally announced two new members, Eric Halvorsen and Andy Barr on the 29th of October and the 7th of November through social media.\n\nThe group released its debut album, ''While the City Sleeps, We Rule the Streets'' in 2006, which contained the single \"[[Snakes on a Plane (Bring It)]]\". In 2007, ''[[\u00a1Viva la Cobra!]]'' was released, which served as the band's first record featuring the complete lineup. ''[[Hot Mess]]'' followed in 2009, reaching commercial success due to the single \"[[Good Girls Go Bad]]\". The band's fourth studio album, ''[[Night Shades]]'' was released August 29, 2011 featuring the top 40 first single \"[[You Make Me Feel...]]\"."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"26058974":{"pageid":26058974,"ns":0,"title":"Cold Blank","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=January 2013}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Cold Blank\n|image = Cold Blank, post split promo photo, Jan 2014.jpg|220px|alt=This promo photo is of solo production outfit Cold Blank, following a recent split of the original duo.\n|caption = Cold Blank in 2014\n|background = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n|origin = Los Angeles, USA\n|instrument = \n|genre = [[House music|House]], [[electro house]], [[progressive house]], [[dubstep]], [[drum and bass]], [[indie dance]], [[nu-disco]]\n|years_active = 2008 \u2013 present\n|label = Burn The Fire Records, [[Vicious Vinyl|Vicious]], [[Dim Mak Records]], [[Ultra Music]], Cr2 Records\n|affiliated labels = Burn The Fire Records, [[Vicious Vinyl|Vicious]]\n|Related_acts = \n|website = \thttp://www.coldblank.com\n|associated_acts = \n|current_members = Christopher Gaspar\n|past_members = Manuel Luquin\n}}'''Cold Blank''' is a Los Angeles\u2013based electronic [[house music]] DJ/production project created by [[United States|American]] DJ/Producer '''Christopher Gaspar'''. Formerly a collaboration along with DJ/producer '''Manuel Luquin''', they parted ways in late 2013.<ref>https://www.facebook.com/coldblank/posts/10151779274545875</ref>\n\nWith early beginnings stemming from the underground party scene in Los Angeles, the former duo launched their company Burn The Fire in 2007 to brand their events and pop-up parties that helped pave the way for the explosion of [[Electronic dance music|EDM]] before they began working together on production.<ref>http://avalonhollywood.com/club-night/control/cold-blank-charlie-darker-at-control/</ref> In autumn of 2009, the Burn The Fire brand evolved into a record label and talent agency. [[Damian Marley]] that climbed up to #1 on Beatport's Top 100 [[Hip Hop]] chart.<ref>http://distilleryimage11.ak.instagram.com/4b182974e81011e183fe22000a1e8a57_7.jpg</ref> Since 2008, Cold Blank has sandwiches| cold cut}}\n{{Refimprove|    date= March 2009}}\n{{Use dmy dates| date=  July 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n    | name             = Coldcut\n    | image            = Matt Black - Coldcut (Vienna 2006).jpg\n    | caption          = Matt Black at a Coldcut performance, 2006\n    | image_size       = <!-- Only for images narrower than 220 pixels -->\n    | background       = group_or_band\n    | alias            = \n    | origin           = [[London]], [[England]]\n    | genre            = [[Electronica]], [[House music|house]], [[Hip hop music|hip hop]], [[trip hop]], [[downtempo]]\n    | years_active     = 1986&ndash;present\n    | label            = [[Ninja Tune]]{{small| (current)}}, {{nowrap| [[Tommy Boy Records|Tommy Boy]]}}, [[Reprise Records|Reprise]], {{nowrap| [[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]]{{small| (former)}}}}\n    | associated_acts= [[DJ Food]], [[Hex (VJ group)|Hex]], [[Hexstatic]], [[Yazz]], {{nowrap| [[Lisa Stansfield]]}}, {{nowrap| [[The Fall (band)|The Fall]]}}\n    | website        = {{url| Coldcut.net| Coldcut.net}}\n    | current_members= \n* [[Matt Black (DJ)|Matt Black]]\n* Jonathan More\n    }}\n\n'''Coldcut''' are an English [[electronic music]] duo composed of [[Matt Black (DJ)|Matt Black]] and Jonathan More. Credited as pioneers for pop sampling in the \u201880s,<ref>{{cite book|title=Spin|url=http://books.google.com/?id=X1aghtVf0GEC&pg=PA48&dq=coldcut+%22Say+Kids+What+Time+Is+It%3F%22&q=coldcut+%22Say+Kids+What+Time+Is+It%3F%22#v=snippet&q=coldcut%20%22Say%20Kids%20What%20Time%20Is%20It%3F%22&f=false|accessdate=1996|author1=Media|first1=Spin L.L.C.|date=1996-12}}</ref> Coldcut are also considered the first stars of UK electronic dance music <ref>{{cite web|title='After 200bpm, your heart blows up'|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2006/jan/18/popandrock|accessdate=2006}}</ref> due to their innovative style, which featured [[cut-up technique|cut-up]] samples of hip-hop, breaks, jazz, spoken word and various other types of music, as well as video and [[multimedia]]. According to ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'', \u201cin \u201987 Coldcut pioneered the British fad for \u2018DJ records\u2019\u201d.<ref name=Spin>{{cite book|title=Spin|url=http://books.google.com/?id=Jq-A2xEoAHIC&lpg=PA86&dq=%22trip-hop%22+coldcut&q=%22trip-hop%22+coldcut#v=snippet&q=%22trip-hop%22%20coldcut&f=false|accessdate=1998|author1=Media|first1=Spin L.L.C.|date=1998-04}}</ref>\n\nColdcut\u2019s records first introduced the public to pop artists [[Yazz]] and [[Lisa Stansfield]],<ref name=\"The Omnibus Book of British and American hit singles, 1960-1990\">{{cite book|title=The Omnibus Book of British and American hit singles, 1960-1990|url=http://books.google.com/?id=YE5LAAAAYAAJ&q=coldcut+%22Doctorin%27+the+House%22&dq=coldcut+%22Doctorin%27+the+House%22|accessdate=1990|author1=McAleer|first1=Dave|date=1990-06}}</ref> through which these artists achieved pop chart success. In addition, Coldcut has remixed and created productions on tracks by the likes of [[Eric B & Rakim]], Yazz, [[James Brown]], [[Queen Latifah]], [[Eurythmics]], [[INXS]], [[Steve Reich]], [[Blondie (band)|Blondie]], [[The Fall (band)|The Fall]], [[Pierre Henri]], [[Nina Simone]], [[Fog]], [[Red Snapper (band)|Red Snapper]], and [[BBC Radiophonic Workshop]].\n\nBeyond their work as a production duo, Coldcut are the founders of [[Ninja Tune]], an independent record label in [[London]], [[England]] (with satellite offices in [[Montreal]] and [[Los Angeles]]) with an overall emphasis on encouraging interactive technology<ref>{{cite book|title=Billboard|url=http://books.google.com/?id=vgcEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA28&dq=Arista+coldcut&q=Arista+coldcut#v=snippet&q=Arista%20coldcut&f=false|accessdate=1996|author1=Nielsen Business Media|first1=Inc|date=1996-09-07}}</ref> and finding innovative uses of [[software]].<ref>{{cite news|title=Music Week|accessdate=August 9, 1997|date=August 9, 1997}}</ref> The label\u2019s first releases (the first four volumes of [[DJ Food]] - 'Jazz Brakes') were produced by Coldcut in the early 90s, and composed of instrumental [[hip-hop]] cuts that led the duo to help pioneer the [[trip-hop]] genre,<ref>{{cite web|title=After 200bpm, your heart blows up|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2006/jan/18/popandrock|publisher=The Guardian|accessdate=January 18, 2006}}</ref> with artists such as Funky Porcini, The Herbaliser and DJ Vadim.<ref>{{cite news|accessdate=August 9, 1997|newspaper=Music Week|date=August 9, 1997}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1840999":{"pageid":1840999,"ns":0,"title":"Colonel Abrams","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP sources|date=November 2010}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Colonel Abrams\n| image               = \n| caption             = \n| image_size          = \n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = \n| alias               = \n| birth_date          = \n| birth_place         = [[Detroit]], [[Michigan]], [[United States]]\n| death_date          = \n| death_place         = \n| origin              = [[New York City, New York]], United States\n| genre               = [[House music|House]], [[Boogie (genre)|boogie]], [[urban contemporary]]\n| instrument          = [[Human voice|Vocals]], [[Guitar]], [[Piano]]\n| occupation          = Singer\n| years_active        = 1960s\u2013present\n| label               = [[MCA Records|MCA]]\n| associated_acts     = \n| website             = \n| current_members     = \n| past_members        = \n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Colonel Abrams''' is an American [[House music|house]] and [[Urban contemporary|urban]] musician, who was born in [[Detroit]], [[Michigan]], and raised in [[New York City, New York]]. Da Mob scored a number-one [[United States|US]] ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Songs|Hot Dance Music/Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]] hit in 1998 with \"[[Fun (Da Mob song)|Fun]]\".<ref>{{cite book |title= Hot Dance/Disco: 1974-2003|last=Whitburn |first=Joel |authorlink=Joel Whitburn |year=2004 |publisher=Record Research |page=98}}</ref> The track was written by Karen Gordon (aka [[Dajae]]), who was supposed to be the featured singer on the single and had recorded a test pressing.  However, a contract dispute between Gordon and Morillo's Subliminal Records, resulted in Brown taking over the vocal duties when the single was released.\n\n\"Fun\" peaked at #33 in the [[UK Singles Chart]] in May 1998, and a follow-up single, \"It's all Good\" reached #54 in the same listing in July 1999.<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 133}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"14744720":{"pageid":14744720,"ns":0,"title":"Dada Life","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{refimprove|date=January 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist  <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Dada Life\n| image               = Image dadalife.jpg\n| landscape           = yes\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Stockholm]], [[Sweden]]\n| genre               = [[Electro house]], [[progressive house]]\n| years_active        = 2006\u2013present\n| label               = [[Dim Mak Records]], Breastfed, [[Ministry of Sound Australia]], Pickadoll, Southern Fried, Prestel, Musical Freedom, So Much Dada\n| website             = {{url|dadalife.com}}\n| current_members = Olle Corn\u00e9er<br />Stefan Engblom\n}}\n\n'''Dada Life''' is a [[Swedish people|Swedish]] [[DJ]] duo from [[Stockholm]]. The duo consists of Olle Corn\u00e9er and Stefan Engblom and was formed in 2006.<ref>{{cite web|title=Dada Life Bio, Music, News & Shows|url=http://djz.com/featured_djs/dada-life/|publisher=DJZ.com|accessdate=March 7, 2013}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"13690082":{"pageid":13690082,"ns":0,"title":"Dada Nada","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{unreferenced|date=July 2013}}\n'''Dada Nada''' - House Music and Hip House act which served as the moniker for [[Robert Ozn]] (born [[Robert M. Rosen]]) after the breakup of New York art rock act  [[EBN-OZN]], an MTV darling in the mid 80s.  Dada Nada had two American Billboard Top 5 Club records in 1989 and 1990: Haunted House and Deep Love, plus additional charted records in Europe particularly in the UK: GIve It All You Got, The Good Thing. Distribution: One Voice Records North America (a start up indie label owned by Ozn) and Polydor/Polygram UK/International. Producers, mixers and writers that worked with the act: [[Frankie Knuckles]] & [[David Morales]], Mike \"Hitman\" Wilson, [[Bad Boy Bill]], Steve Wight and Bob Greenberg. \n\nDada Nada/Robert Ozn was credited with the first House record by a white artist to chart on a major chart in the US,  Haunted House (MTV News).  \n\nIn particular Dada Nada was recognized for his combination of white rap and sung vocals over House tracks and even more importantly for his integration of Deep House and Acid House into a pop songwriting format. \n\nDada Nada toured the US in 1990 and suffered a gang related shooting in the audience during a performance in Chicago.  Robert Ozn left the music business shortly thereafter.\n\nHe works in the film industry as a producer/screenwriter with three films to his credit: \"I Witness\" starring [[Jeff Daniels]], [[James Spader]], [[Portia de Rossi]], and [[Clifton Collins, Jr.]]; \"Earth's Final Hours\" for The Sy Fy Channel and \"Turned Towards the Sun,\" about British aristocrat, war hero and out bisexual [[Michael Burn]], which premiered at the British Film Institute. \n\nDada Nada lives in Vancouver, Rio de Janeiro and Los Angeles.\n\n[[Category:American house musicians]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"168310":{"pageid":168310,"ns":0,"title":"Daft Punk","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=April 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name            = Daft Punk<!--SEE DISCUSSION ON LOGO-->\n| image           = Daftpunklapremiere2010.jpg<!--SEE DISCUSSION ON IMAGE-->\n| image_size      = 250px\n| landscape       = <!-- yes, if wide image, otherwise leave blank -->\n| alt             = \n| caption         = Daft Punk at the premiere of ''[[Tron: Legacy]]'' in 2010. From left: [[Thomas Bangalter]], [[Guy-Manuel de Homem-Christo]]\n| background      = group_or_band\n| alias           = \n| origin          = Paris, France\n| genre           = [[French house]]<ref>{{cite news|title=Electro Music Ambassador's French Touch|url=http://www.nytimes.com/2012/01/27/arts/27iht-pedrowinter27.html?pagewanted=all|newspaper=The New York Times}}</ref>\n| years_active    = {{start date|1993}}\u2013present<ref>{{cite web|url=https://itunes.apple.com/ca/artist/daft-punk/id5468295 |title=iTunes \u2013 Music \u2013 Daft Punk |publisher=iTunes Store |accessdate=13 May 2013}}</ref>\n| label           = [[Soma Quality Recordings|Soma]], [[Virgin Records|Virgin]], [[Walt Disney Records|Walt Disney]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]] \n| associated_acts = <!--SEE DISCUSSION ON ACTS-->[[Darlin' (French band)|Darlin']], [[Stardust (band)|Stardust]], [[Together (French band)|Together]], [[Crydamoure|Le Knight Club]]\n| website         = {{URL|daftpunk.com}}\n| current_members = [[Thomas Bangalter]]<br />[[Guy-Manuel de Homem-Christo]]\n| past_members    = \n}}'''Daft Punk''' is a French<!--Please don't add awards to the lead sentence. Listing awards here highlights them over other content in the article, therefore violating the neutral point of view policy. Thank you.--> [[electronic music]] duo consisting of musicians [[Guy-Manuel de Homem-Christo]] and [[Thomas Bangalter]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Daft Punk Bio, Music, News & Shows|url=http://djz.com/featured_djs/daft-punk/|publisher=DJZ.com|accessdate=7 March 2013}}</ref><ref name=HouseSynthpop/><ref name=Allmusic>[http://www.allmusic.com/artist/daft-punk-p168791 Daft Punk Allmusic bio]</ref><ref name=\"MusiqueVol.1\" /> Daft Punk reached significant popularity in the late 1990s [[house music|house]] movement in France and met with continued success in the years following, combining elements of house with [[synthpop]].<ref name=HouseSynthpop>{{cite news| url= http://www.telegraph.co.uk/culture/music/3669339/Daft-Punk-Behind-the-robot-masks.html | title= Daft Punk: Behind the robot masks| first= Bernadette | last= McNulty | work=The Telegraph |date=17 November 2007 | accessdate= 14 October 2012}}</ref><ref name=Allmusic/><ref name=\"Mixmag 2006\" /> The duo's songs are considered essential in the [[French house]] scene. The group was managed from 1996 to 2008 by [[Pedro Winter]] (Busy P), the head of [[Ed Banger Records]].<ref name=\"Pedro\" /> Early in the group's career, the band members were influenced by groups including [[The Beach Boys]] and [[The Rolling Stones]].<ref name=\"DarlinBio\" />\n\nBangalter and de Homem-Christo were originally in a band called [[Darlin' (French band)|Darlin']], which disbanded after a short period of time, leaving the two to experiment musically on their own. The duo became Daft Punk, releasing its debut album ''[[Homework (Daft Punk album)|Homework]]'' in 1997 to highly positive reviews. The 2001 release of ''[[Discovery (Daft Punk album)|Discovery]]'' was even more successful, driven by the club singles \"[[One More Time (Daft Punk song)|One More Time]]\", \"[[Digital Love]]\", and \"[[Harder, Better, Faster, Stronger]]\". In March 2005, the duo released the album ''[[Human After All]]'' to mixed reviews. However, the singles \"[[Robot Rock (song)|Robot Rock]]\" and \"[[Technologic]]\" achieved success in the United Kingdom.\n\nDaft Punk [[Alive 2006/2007|toured throughout 2006 and 2007]] and released the live album ''[[Alive 2007]]'', which won a [[Grammy Award for Best Electronic/Dance Album]]. The duo composed the score of the film ''[[Tron: Legacy]]'' and in 2010 released the [[Tron: Legacy (soundtrack)|soundtrack album of the film]]. In January 2013, Daft Punk left [[EMI Records]] for [[Sony Music Entertainment]]'s subsidiary label [[Columbia Records|Columbia]], and released ''[[Random Access Memories]]'' in 2013 to worldwide critical acclaim. The lead single \"[[Get Lucky (Daft Punk song)|Get Lucky]]\" became an international success, peaking in the top 10 in 32 countries. ''Random Access Memories'' led to five Grammy wins in 2014 including [[Grammy Award for Album of the Year|Album of the Year]], as well as [[Grammy Award for Record of the Year|Record of the Year]] for \"Get Lucky\".\n\nThe group is known for emphasising using visual and story components associated with their musical productions, and for using disguises while in public and/or performing; specifically ornate helmets and gloves to assume [[robot]] personas in most of their public appearances since 2001. personality]], [[record label]] owner, and [[music critic]] from [[Chicago]], which is widely considered the birthplace of [[House music]].  He currently resides in [[Los Angeles]] as of 2009.\n\nHe is primarily known for electronic dance music, with productions appearing in the compilations of [[Nick Warren]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Nick Warren returns to The Masters Series for his 1st solo Renaissance album|url=http://renaissance.dj/blog/2012/12/nick-warren-solo-masters-series-debut/|accessdate=December 2012}}</ref> [[Hernan Cattaneo]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Darin Epsilon - Red Matter|url=http://www.trackitdown.net/track/darin-epsilon/red-matter/house/5612234.html|accessdate=6 May 2013}}</ref> [[Armin van Buuren]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Get Armin\u2019s ASOT600 warm-up sets on Spotify!|url=https://www.astateoftrance.com/news/get-armins-asot600-warm-up-sets-on-spotify/|accessdate=April 2013}}</ref> [[Markus Schulz]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Markus Schulz - Global DJ Broadcast Top 15 - October 2011|url=http://www.beatport.com/release/global-dj-broadcast-top-15-october-2011-including-classic-bonus-track/681402|accessdate=7 October 2011}}</ref> and [[Paul Oakenfold]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Paul Oakenfold \u2013 Perfecto Vegas|url=http://www.discogs.com/Paul-Oakenfold-Perfecto-Vegas/release/1840101|accessdate=7 July 2009}}</ref> among many others.  His music has appeared on film and television, and is used by global brands such as [[MTV]],<ref>{{cite web|title=Jersey Shore \" Season 2 \" Songs From the Show \" Ep. 212|url=http://www.mtv.com/shows/jersey_shore/season_2/episode_music.jhtml?episodeID=171240|accessdate=October 2010}}</ref> American DJ, American Audio, and Elation Professional.  USL Magazine proclaimed him ''\"King of Progressive House\"'' in May 2012,<ref>{{cite web|first=Drew|title=Darin Epsilon Is King Of Progressive House Music|url=http://www.uslmag.com/2012/05/11/dj-darin-epsilon-is-king-of-progressive-house-music/|accessdate=11 May 2012}}</ref> and Clubbing9ine.com referred to him as ''\"North America\u2019s leading figure in pure Progressive House\"'' in December 2012.<ref>{{cite web|title=Darin Epsilon\u2019s Phenomenal Finish to 2012|url=http://www.clubbing9ine.com/news/darin-epsilons-phenomenal-finish-to-2012/|accessdate=18 December 2012}}</ref>\n\nHe currently hosts a monthly radio show and podcast called '''Perspectives'''.  Established in November 2006, the show is split into two parts, with the first being his own 60 minute set, followed by a guest mix from an established artist.  Perspectives has allowed him to feature dozens of respected names in the industry including [[Darren Emerson]] (formerly of [[Underworld (band)]]), [[Max Graham]], [[Robert Babicz]], [[Max Cooper (electronica musician)|Max Cooper]], [[Guy J]], [[Jody Wisternoff]] (one-half [[Way Out West (group)|Way Out West]] with [[Nick Warren]]), and many more.  The first broadcasts were on [[Digitally Imported]] (DI.fm), but the program has since moved to Frisky Radio.  His record label [[Perspectives Digital]] was launched in November 2010 as an extension of the brand, further solidifying his influence and presence within the global dance community.<ref>{{cite web|title=About {{!}} Perspectives Digital|url=http://www.perspectivesdigital.com/about/}}</ref>\n\nDuring the summer of 2011, [[John Digweed]] named Darin as one of the winners in his 'Structures' DJ Mix Competition, sponsored by [[Bedrock]] and [[Ableton Live]].<ref>{{cite web|title=John Digweed announces \"Structures\" mix competition winners|url=http://news.beatport.com/blog/2011/08/12/john-digweed-announces-structures-mix-competition-winners/|accessdate=12 August 2011}}</ref>  The all-star panel of judges consisted of [[Oliver Lieb]], [[Nick Muir]], Gavin Kingsley ([[King Unique]]), [[Robert Babicz]], and Digweed himself.  Contestants were required to put together their best 25 to 30 minute mix using the tracks that appeared on the 'Structures Two' compilation.  To make it even more special, 'Structures' DJ tools were included to weave into their sets.\n\nAs a DJ, he has shared the stage with many of dance music\u2019s superstars including [[Hernan Cattaneo]], [[Nick Warren]], [[John Digweed]], [[Sasha (DJ)|Sasha]], [[James Zabiela]], [[Armin van Buuren]], [[Above & Beyond (band)|Above & Beyond]], [[Markus Schulz]], [[Ferry Corsten]], [[BT (musician)|BT]], and countless others.  He has performed at North America\u2019s biggest festivals including [[Beyond Wonderland]], [[White Wonderland]], [[Nocturnal Wonderland]], and [[Ultra Music Festival]].  He has also been invited to headline shows in [[Argentina]], [[Kenya]], [[Russia]], [[United Kingdom]], [[Canada]], [[Brazil]], [[Mexico]], [[Bulgaria]], [[Colombia]], [[Peru]], [[Dominican Republic]], and [[Costa Rica]].<ref>{{cite web|title=Biography {{!}} Darin Epsilon|url=http://darinepsilon.com/about/}}</ref>\n\nAsides from focusing on his own career, Darin has a monthly column in [[Tilllate]] (formerly [[M8 Magazine]]), where he reviews new releases in the [[Progressive House]] and [[Tech House]] genres. He co-founded Gum Productions and released his first album, ''[[Just a Little More Love]]'', in 2002. Later, he released ''[[Guetta Blaster]]'' (2004) and ''[[Pop Life (David Guetta album)|Pop Life]]'' (2007) featuring 2 tracks with the UK's [[Tara McDonald]].\n\nGuetta achieved mainstream success with his 2009 album ''[[One Love (David Guetta album)|One Love]]'' which included the hit singles \"[[When Love Takes Over]]\", \"[[Gettin' Over You]]\", and \"[[Sexy Bitch]]\", all three of which reached #1 in the [[United Kingdom]], and \"[[Memories (David Guetta song)|Memories]]\". The 2011 followup album, ''[[Nothing but the Beat]]'', continued this success, containing the hit singles \"[[Where Them Girls At]]\", \"[[Little Bad Girl]]\", \"[[Without You (David Guetta song)|Without You]]\", \"[[Titanium (song)|Titanium]]\" and \"[[Turn Me On (David Guetta song)|Turn Me On]]\".\n\nGuetta has sold over nine million albums and 30 million singles worldwide.<ref>{{cite web|last=Otter|first=Charlotte|title=F*** Me I'm Famous goes global<!--The original article title has \"F\" followed by three \"*\". (pronounced \"dead mouse\"), is a Canadian [[progressive house|progressive]]-[[house music]] producer and performer from [[Toronto]], Ontario.\n\nZimmerman produces a variety of styles within the house genre and sometimes other forms of electronic dance music. His tracks have been included in numerous compilation albums such as the 2007 ''[[In Search of Sunrise 6: Ibiza]]'' CD. The February 2008 issue of ''[[Mixmag]]''{{'}}s music magazine included a free CD which was titled ''MixMag Presents: The Hottest New Name In Dance! DEADMAU5 Tech-Trance-Electro-Madness'', mixed by Zimmerman. Tracks have also been included and presented on [[Armin van Buuren]]'s ''[[A State of Trance]]'' radio show. His debut album, ''[[Get Scraped]]'', was released in 2005, followed by others in the next few years.\n\nAs well as his own solo releases, Zimmerman has worked alongside other DJs and producers, such as [[Kaskade]], MC Flipside, [[Rob Swire]] of [[Knife Party]] and [[Pendulum (band)|Pendulum]], [[Wolfgang Gartner]], Bighorse, and on a number of releases, he has partnered with [[Melleefresh]]. The group's best-known [[single (music)|single]] was \"[[Groove Is in the Heart]]\", which was released from their 1990 debut [[album]], ''[[World Clique]]'', and was a Top 10 hit in multiple countries. That song notably featured [[Funk music|funk]] musician [[Bootsy Collins]], a fan of the group. Deee-Lite scored six number-one [[hit record|hits]] on the U.S. ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Songs|Hot Dance Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]] over their history. Based in [[Washington, D.C.]], Shirazinia and Tayebi are well known for providing house or dance [[remix]]es of tracks of famous stars such as [[Madonna (entertainer)|Madonna]], [[Janet Jackson]], [[Cher]] and [[Gabrielle (singer)|Gabrielle]], and for their live DJing sets. Their collaborations and remixing abilities first came to attention with their seminal 1995 remix of De'Lacy's \"Hideaway.\" Deep Dish's album ''[[Junk Science (album)|Junk Science]]'' was released in 1998. The duo was nominated for a [[Grammy]] for [[Madonna (entertainer)|Madonna]]'s \"Music,\" and won a \"Best Remixed Recording\" Grammy for their remix of [[Dido (singer)|Dido]]'s \"Thank You.\"<ref>{{cite web|url=http://dancemusic.about.com/cs/interviews/a/IntDeepDishAli.htm |title=Interview with Ali of Deep Dish |publisher=Dancemusic.about.com |date=2012-06-20 |accessdate=2014-08-27}}</ref> In 2006, the DJs disbanded and moved to solo careers. '''Dev''' (sometimes stylized as '''DEV''' or '''dEV'''), is an American rapper, singer and songwriter. She was discovered by the record label, Indie-Pop, and [[The Cataracs]] via [[Myspace]] after her friend Shane Crislip, posted her singing to some beats. Dev's song \"[[Booty Bounce]]\" was sampled in [[Far East Movement]]'s hit single \"[[Like a G6]]\" which reached number 1 in the US, and sold over four million downloads in the country.\n\nDev was signed to [[Universal Republic]] in October 2010, and released her debut single \"[[Bass Down Low]]\" in November 16, 2010. She was scheduled to release her debut album ''[[The Night the Sun Came Up]]'' on September 5, 2011. The album was pushed back and was released in the United States on March 27, 2012. At one point a [[cheerleader]] for the [[Tampa Bay Buccaneers]], she got her start performing in the bands Hi-Octane,Trama and Maxx.  During her tenure with MAXX she was courted by Alan Walden (Capricorn Records/Hustler Productions) before launching a solo career.<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p51146|pure_url=yes}} Biography], Allmusic.com</ref> She also sang backup on tour for [[Gloria Estefan]] for nine years. Her first disc was the [[Lou Pace]]-[[record producer|produced]] 1986 [[album]], ''Perfect Timing'', and over the next few years she launched several hits on the [[United States|US]] ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Songs|Hot Dance/Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]]. She had two [[Top 40|Top 10]] hits in the [[UK Singles Chart]] with \"Serious\" (1987, #8) and \"Joy and Pain\" (1989, #10).<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 20}}</ref> 1995's \"Real\", her last US chart hit, was taken from the [[soundtrack]] to the [[Sylvester Stallone]] film ''[[The Specialist]]''.  The [[United Kingdom|UK]] dance act [[Strike (band)|Strike]] used her chorus hook line from \"Serious\", as the basis for their club hit, \"[[U Sure Do]]\", that same year. In 2009, \"He is the Joy\" appeared on the ''[[Precious (soundtrack)|Precious]]'' soundtrack."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"149561":{"pageid":149561,"ns":0,"title":"Donna Summer","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=May 2013}}\n{{tone|date=December 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name        = Donna Summer\n| image       = Nobel Peace Price Concert 2009 Donna Summer3.jpg\n| caption     = Summer in December 2009\n| background  = solo_singer\n| alias       = Queen of Disco<br/>Donna Gaines \n| birth_name  = LaDonna Adrian Gaines\n| birth_date  = {{birth date|1948|12|31|mf=yes}}\n| birth_place = [[Boston, Massachusetts]], United States\n| death_date  = {{death date and age|2012|5|17|1948|12|31|mf=yes}}\n| death_place = [[Naples, Florida]]\n| genre       = {{flatlist|\n*[[Pop music|Pop]]\n*[[disco]]\n*[[Dance music|dance]]\n*[[Rock music|rock]]\n*[[New wave music|new wave]]\n*[[Rhythm and blues|R&B]]\n*[[funk]]\n*[[Gospel music|gospel]]\n*[[Soul music|soul]]}}\n| occupation  = {{flatlist|\n* Singer\n* songwriter\n* [[Painting|painter]]}}\n| years_active = 1968\u20132012\n| instrument  = Vocals\n| label       = {{flatlist|\n*[[Oasis Records|Oasis]]\n*[[Casablanca Records|Casablanca]]\n*[[Geffen Records|Geffen]]\n*[[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]]\n*[[Mercury Records|Mercury]]\n*[[Warner Music Group|WEA]]\n*[[Epic Records|Epic]]\n*[[Burgundy Records|Burgundy]]}}\n| associated_acts = {{flatlist|\n*[[Giorgio Moroder]]\n*[[Brooklyn Dreams (group)|Brooklyn Dreams]]}}\n}}\n\n'''LaDonna Adrian Gaines''' (December 31, 1948{{spaced ndash}}May 17, 2012),<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p5556/biography|pure_url=yes}} allmusic (((Donna Summer > Biography )))]</ref> known by her stage name, '''Donna Summer''', was an American singer, songwriter, and painter. She gained prominence during the [[disco]] era of the late 1970s. A five-time [[Grammy Award]] winner, she was the first artist to have three consecutive double albums reach No. 1 on the United States ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' album chart and charted four number-one singles in the United States within a 12-month period. Summer has reportedly sold over 140 million records, making her one of the [[List of best-selling music artists|world's best-selling artists of all time]].<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.vervemusicgroup.com/donnasummer|publisher=vervemusic.com|title=vervemusic.com|accessdate=November 11, 2014}}</ref>\n\nWhile influenced by the [[counterculture of the 1960s]], she became the front singer of a [[psychedelic rock]] band named Crow and moved to New York City. Joining a touring version of the musical ''[[Hair (musical)|Hair]]'', she left New York and spent several years living, acting, and singing in Europe, where she met music producers, [[Giorgio Moroder]] and [[Pete Bellotte]].\n\nShe returned to the United States, in 1975 with mass commercial success of the song [[Love to Love You Baby (song)|Love to Love You Baby]]. Over the following years Summer followed this success with a string of other hits, such as \"[[I Feel Love]]\", \"[[Last Dance (song)|Last Dance]]\", \"[[MacArthur Park (song)|MacArthur Park]]\", \"[[Heaven Knows (Donna Summer song)|Heaven Knows]]\", \"[[Hot Stuff (Donna Summer song)|Hot Stuff]]\", \"[[Bad Girls (Donna Summer song)|Bad Girls]]\", \"[[Dim All the Lights]]\", \"[[No More Tears (Enough Is Enough)]]\", and \"[[On the Radio (Donna Summer song)|On the Radio]]\". \"Last Dance\" won an Academy Award and a Golden Globe for Best Original Song on the \"Thank God It's Friday\" movie soundtrack. She became known as the \"Queen of Disco\", while her music gained a global following.<ref name=\"The Times\">{{cite news |title=Obituaries: Donna Summer |year=2012 |journal=The Times |location=London |publisher=News Corporation |page=53 |ref=Tim12}}</ref>\n\nSummer died on May 17, 2012, at her home in [[Naples, Florida]].<ref>{{cite web|last=Sherman|first=Catherine|url=http://www.zillow.com/blog/2012-05-21/donna-summers-lasting-real-estate-legacy|title=Donna Summer's Lasting (Real Estate) Legacy|publisher=Zillow.com|date=May 21, 2012|accessdate=April 13, 2013}}</ref> In her obituary in ''[[The Times]]'', Summer was described as the \"undisputed queen of the Seventies disco boom\" who reached the status of \"one of the world's leading female singers.\"<ref name=\"The Times\"/> Moroder described Summer's work with him on the song \"I Feel Love\" as \"really the start of [[electronic dance music|electronic dance]]\" One of the projects of the late 1980s, founded  Ian Bland, with American singer Debbie sharp they performed initially at local events in the English rave clubs such as Shelley's.\n\nIn early 1992, the project gained their first [[hit single]] with \"Feel So Real\", which peaked at #23 in the [[UK Singles Chart]].<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited \n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 168}}</ref> Shortly thereafter, \"Take Me\" reached #39 in the [[United Kingdom|UK]] [[record chart|chart]]. He has remixed Madonna's \"Superstar\" single for Live Nation/Interscope and has released \"U Make Me Wanna\" with Kimberly Cole ft. Garza on Big Beat Records.\n \nHe collaborated with Kimberly Cole and rapper Garza on dance pop tune \"Arrow Through My Heart\" released on August 2, 2011 on Citrusonic \nStereophonic/Crystal Ship Music. This was the first collaboration for the three artists and producer Jeeve. \"Arrow\" reached #16 on the [[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]] Dance Chart.{{citation needed|date=July 2012}}\n \nIn 2011, Eddie Amador partnered up with Orlando Puerta and started '''Citrusonic Label Group''', where he has several artists and projects in development including The Kissboyz, Graph Gonzales and Warren Nomi.{{citation needed|date=July 2012}}\n \nAmador's productions in 2011 included \"Spirituality\" on Erick Morillo\u2019s Subliminal label and 10 Lil Indians on Amador's imprint, Citrusonic Recordings. Eddie's records are supported by well-known DJs including [[David Guetta]], [[Kaskade]], Annie Nightingale,  D.O.N.S., Robbie Rivera, Thomas Gold, and others. His record \"We Are the Beautiful Ones\" is co-produced with [[Harry Romero|Harry \"Choo Choo\" Romero]], and vocalist Countre Black released on Subliminal. A new remix of \"We Are the Beautiful Ones\" by Sympho Nympho (Erick Morillo, Harry Romero and Jose Nunez) will appear on the latest Subliminal Compilation for WMC 2012. Eddie also teamed up with Automatic Panic on \"Morning After\" the current single on his Citrusonic Recordings imprint supported by Mark Knight, Steve Aoki and Judge Jules.\n \nAmador's fame started in 1998 when he penned the \"not everyone understands\", \"house music, it's a spiritual thing, a body thing, a soul thing\". He set them to a hypnotic pulsating beat and the seminal dance classic \"House Music\" was born. It went on to become a global hit and secured Amador an album deal with Deep Dish's Yoshitoshi label. However, it was his next single \"Rise\" that proved his appeal as entered the UK Top 20 giving him exposure as an international class DJ with him performing at famous club venues like Ministry of Sound, The Queen, Centro Fly, Crobar, Stereo as well as Pacha & Space in Ibiza. Based on his success, he set up a second studio in Amsterdam in 2003 where he continued productions for Defected, Nero, and Yoshitoshi. \n \nIn 2007 he began remixing for Leela James, [[Michael Bubl\u00e9]] and [[Seal (musician)|Seal]] for Warner Bros. Records and Reprise Records. He became part of the exclusive group to remix Madonna and his mix of \"Give It to Me\" from ''Hard Candy'' reached #1 on Billboards Hot Dance Club Play Chart. He has gone on to remix [[Yoko Ono]], The Veronicas, [[Alanis Morissette]], [[Audio Playground]], Sliimy, [[Donna Summer]], [[Chris Willis]], [[Kimberly Cole]], [[Jason Derulo]], Kerli, Blush, and many many more.{{citation needed|date=December 2012}}"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"24538456":{"pageid":24538456,"ns":0,"title":"Edward Maya","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| image = \n| caption =\n| image_size = \n| background = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name=Eduard Marian Ilie\n| birth_date = {{Birth date and age|df=yes|1986|6|29}}<ref>[http://www.nrj.fr/music-509/fiches-artistes-522/artiste/bio/12938-edward-maya.html Biographie Edward Maya : bio, parcours artistique Edward Maya \u2013 NRJ<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref>\n| origin = [[Bucharest]], Romania\n| genre = [[House music|House]], [[Electro music|electronic]]\n| instrument = Vocals, accordion, guitar, flute, piano, bagpipes\n| occupation = Musician, dj, record producer, performer, singer/songwriter\n| years_active = 2006\u2013present\n| label = Mayavin Records\n| associated_acts = [[Vika Jigulina]]\n| website = {{url|www.edwardmaya.com}}\n}}\n\n'''Edward Maya''' (born '''Eduard Marian Ilie'''; 29 June 1986) is a Romanian DJ, musician, producer, performer, and composer. He is known for his energetic and danceable mix of grooves, as well as his enthusiastic interaction with the crowd.\n\nBiography Erick Eerdhuizen\n\nIt\u2019s 2011: ever-active Erick Eerdhuizen is passionate, dedicated and energetic when it comes to working on his career as a DJ, composer and producer.\n\nAfter winning \u2018The Dutch DMC Championships\u2019, in 1989, Erick was the official Dutch representative during the World Championships at The Royal Albert Hall in London.\nHe fell in love with a new music genre and consequently made considerable contributions to the upcoming Dutch house culture, creating for example house classics such as \u2018Pancake-Don\u2019t Turn Your Back\u2019, released on record label WORK.\n\nHe established his name as a DJ more firmly during the mid-nineties, landing the Saturday residency at the legendary Amsterdam Club RoXY. There, his infamous SWET nights caused long waiting lines at the door and it pushed Erick\u2019s popularity to new heights. He frequently graced the decks at the main stages of large festivals such as \u2018Dance Valley, \u2018Sensation\u2019 (international residency), \u2018Mysteryland\u2019, \u2018Day At The Park\u2019 and \u2018Extrema Outdoor\u2019. International clubs such as NOW & WOW Rotterdam, Amnesia Ibiza, Rex Paris and Catwalk Barcelona invited him repeatedly, knowing Erick would deliver a full house.\n\nWith an artistic brain and an insatiable lust for music he managed to gain success with international releases, top 10 chart positions, an impressive series of mix compilations and number 1 hit records. Now, a decade into the new century, he\u2019s mostly known as DJ Erick E and he considers himself to be fortunate: Erick won the people\u2019s vote and is leading the number one spot at \u2018DJGuide.nl\u2019 for the last 3 consecutive years.\n\nIn 2010, DJ performances had changed drastically and Eerdhuizen found himself longing for a different approach. A strong desire to return to a basis, founded at Club RoXY, kept growing. He craved for longer sets (\u2018all nighters\u2019) and a more intimate playground, where he could perform a mix of \u2018warm tech-house\u2019 and \u2018danceable techno\u2019.\nThe introduction of E5H \u2013 meaning Erick E 5 Hours \u2013 gave him the chance to control the night from the first until the very last record played. He took the challenge and conquered a demanding crowd during his first E5H gigs at the \u2018Amsterdam Sugar Factory, Bunker NDSM and Westerunie\u2019. Now, the E5H-tour has officially started around smaller venues and popstages, playing \u2018De Effenaar Eindhoven, Paard van Troje The Hague, Mezz Breda and Patronaat Haarlem\u2019 amongst others.\nIn 2011, Eerdhuizen will add a new branch to the tree. Next to his tour, the last 6 months were all about the joy of making music and studio time, where passion and inspiration ran wild. New collabs, steamy productions and the birth of \u2018SMAAKSTOF\u2019 - a brand new record label - are at hand. The first releases under his \u2018tech-house\u2019 alias Eerdhuizen are scheduled for spring, so \u2026better tie your shoe laces and brace yourselves for energy, substance and unbridled passion: Erick Eerdhuizen is going back to basics!"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"1836257":{"pageid":1836257,"ns":0,"title":"Erick Morillo","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- For individuals; see Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Erick Morillo\n| image               = 10.11.12ErickMorilloByLuigiNovi1.jpg\n| alt                 = \n| caption             = Erick Morillo in the dedication ceremony, October 2012\n| image_size          = \n| background          = non_performing_personnel\n| birth_name          = Erick Morillo\n| alias               = \n| birth_date          = {{birth year and age|1971|mf=yes}}<ref name=AllMusic>Birchmeier, Jason. Group members are [[Michael Gray (DJ)|Michael Gray]] and [[Jon Pearn]].  \n\nThey have appeared in the US [[Hot Dance Music/Club Play]] chart three times with their own singles, first under the name [[Arizona (dance music act)|Arizona]] feat. [[Zeeteah Massiah|Zeitia]] with \"Slide On The Rhythm\", which reached number one in 1993, and with \"America (I Love America)\" under the Full Intention name, a number one hit from 1996.  They are also perhaps most well known for their remix of the 1995 club classic \"So In Love\" by Duke. Although many of their remixes for other artists have been successful club hits, they did not return to the chart as artists until 2002, when \"I'll Be Waiting\" featuring [[Shena]] reached number three{{where?|date=June 2013}}.
