Her unconventional image includes short tight curls and an eye patch or sunglasses{{mdash}}she has [[Ptosis (eyelid)|ptosis]], the drooping of one eyelid.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.funtrivia.com/askft/Question89418.html|title=Is the pop singer Gabrielle blind? She never shows her eyes.|publisher=Funtrivia.com|accessdate=2012-05-14}}</ref>\n\nHer debut single \"[[Dreams (Gabrielle song)|Dreams]]\" topped the [[UK Singles Chart]] in June 1993. Other notable singles include \"Going Nowhere\", \"Give Me a Little More Time\", \"[[Walk On By (song)|Walk On By]]\" and \"If You Ever\" \u2013 a duet with [[East 17]]. After a few quiescent years Gabrielle made a stunning comeback with \"Rise\", which became Gabrielle's second UK number one in 2000. The album of the same name also reached the top spot in the [[UK Albums Chart]], where it stayed for three weeks. The successful \"[[Out of Reach (song)|Out of Reach]]\" from the soundtrack to the film ''[[Bridget Jones's Diary (film)|Bridget Jones's Diary]]'', reached number four in the UK Singles Chart. Gabrielle's greatest hits collection, ''[[Dreams Can Come True, Greatest Hits Vol. 1]]'' was released in 2001.\n\nGabrielle has won two [[BRIT Awards]], the first in 1994 for British Breakthrough Act, and the second in 1997 for Best British Female.<ref name=\"British Hit Singles & Albums\">{{cite book\n| first= David\n| last= Roberts\n| year= 2006\n| title= British Hit Singles & Albums\n| edition= 19th\n| publisher= Guinness World Records Limited\n| location= London\n| isbn= 1-904994-10-5\n| page= 219}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"405587":{"pageid":405587,"ns":0,"title":"General Levy","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=December 2014}}\n{{BLP sources|date=February 2011}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| image               =\n| name                = General Levy\n| caption             =\n| image_size          =\n| background          = solo_singer\n| birth_name          = Paul Levy\n| alias               =\n| birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|df=yes|1971|4|28}}\n| birth_place         = London, England\n| death_date          =\n| death_place         =\n| instrument          = Vocals\n| genre               = [[Ragga]], [[oldschool jungle|jungle]]\n| occupation          = Musician\n| years_active        =1988 \u2013 present\n| label               =\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             =\n| notable_instruments =\n}}\n\n'''General Levy''' (born '''Paul Levy''', 28 April 1971, London, England) is an English [[ragga]] [[Deejay (Jamaican)|deejay]], regularly employed on studio tracks by [[drum and bass]] DJs. Experience\n| website             = [http://www.grantnelson.net/ grantnelson.net]\n| current_members     = \n| past_members        = \n| notable_instruments = Keyboards\n}}\n\n'''Grant Nelson''' (born 27 April 1971 in London), also known as '''Wishdokta''', '''Bump & Flex''' and '''N'n'G''', is an English DJ, [[remix]]er and record producer.<ref>{{cite news|first =Larry|last =Flick|title=Dance Trax|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=8AkEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA29&dq=%22grant+nelson%22+dj&hl=en&ei=Qm44TbuaOY6CsQPBwsiQAw&sa=X&oi=book_result&ct=result&resnum=2&ved=0CDIQ6AEwAQ#v=onepage&q=%22grant%20nelson%22%20dj&f=false|accessdate=20 January 2011|newspaper=Billboard|date=8 August 1998}}</ref>\n\nNelson is heralded as one of the godfathers of [[UK garage]] due to his numerous club hits on his Nice 'n' Ripe record label in the early 1990s. It was his sound along with a few others that gave birth to the then known as 'Sunday Scene' which evolved into UK garage.\n\nHe also produced under the name \"Wishdokta\" from 1990 to 1993 when he was producing [[breakbeat hardcore]]/[[drum and bass]] for the legendary London label [[Kickin Records]].\n\nIn 1993, Wishdokta teamed up with DJ Vibes and together they delivered some of [[happy hardcore]]'s biggest anthems on Vibes' Asylum Music Inc. and other labels including Happy Trax.\n\nIn 1997, Nelson started using the alter-ego \"Bump & Flex\" and began to produce [[2-step garage|UK 2-step]]. He delivered some of the scene's biggest records including \"Funk on Ah Roll\" by [[James Brown]].\n\nNelson has always remained a [[house music|house]] head since his early Nice 'n' Ripe days and continues to do so to the present with his Swing City Records label that consistently delivers top drawer house music.\n\nSome of the artists Nelson has remixed and worked with include [[Kelis]], [[Jodeci]], [[Mis-Teeq]], [[Aaliyah]], [[James Brown]], [[Artful Dodger (UK band)|The Artful Dodger]], [[Jamiroquai]], [[Lutricia McNeal]], [[Thelma Houston]], [[Another Level (band)|Another Level]], [[Goldie]], [[Roy Ayers]], [[Guy (band)|Guy]], [[Rosie Gaines]], [[Juliet Roberts]], [[Liberty X]], [[Towa Tei]], [[Evelyn \"Champagne\" King]], [[Bebel Gilberto]], [[Negrocan]], [[Beverley Knight]], [[Brand New Heavies]], [[Faithless]], [[Simply Red]], [[Frankie Knuckles]] and [[Agnes Carlsson|Agnes]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"22130882":{"pageid":22130882,"ns":0,"title":"The Greenskeepers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Greenskeepers]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"16320553":{"pageid":16320553,"ns":0,"title":"Gregory Del Piero","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Gregory Del Piero\n| image                 =\n| caption            = Gregory Del Piero\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist   \n| birth_place                = [[S\u00e8te]], France\n| birth_date                = {{Birth date|1972|10|14}}\n| genre               = [[Deep House]]/[[Gospel House]]/[[Dance music|Dance]]\n| occupation          = [[Music Producer]]/[[DJ]]\n| years_active        = 1987 -present\n| label               = Del Records\n| website                 = [http://www.gregorydelpiero.com Gregory Del Piero] Official Site\n\n}}\n\n'''Gregory Del Piero''' (born October 14, 1972 in [[S\u00e8te]], [[H\u00e9rault]]) is a French music producer and [[DJ]].\n\nIn 1987, Gregory Del Piero started as a [[DJ]], he was introduced to the night-life scene by one of his uncles who was a bouncer at the time.  The following decade Gregory worked as a resident dj in numerous popular clubs in the south of France until  the summer of 1998, where  he met the world famous [[Joe Claussell]] of Body & Soul, from New York City, while Joe was on tour in France.  After that meeting Gregory decided to pursue his interest in electronic music and moved to San Francisco.\n\nIn 2000, through the club scene and Mauricio Aviles, he was introduced to Israel Megerssa the owner of Zebra Records.  Israel took Gregory under his wing and hired him as a house music buyer at Zebra Records Music store.  More than a father figure, Israel was a spiritual guide to Gregory and told Gregory that he should start getting into music production.  That will mark the beginning of a 4 year collaboration with the keyboardist and sound engineer Charles Spencer where Gregory began producing his signature sound \u2013 [[Soul music|soulful]] [[house music]].\n\nIn 2001, Gregory's first single, titled \"Don't Hesitate\", was signed by the label Subliminal Records and since then he has produced some of the most influential and cutting-edge \"master pieces\" in the industry, such as his remix for [[Miguel Migs]] & [[Jay-J]] \"Friend of the Blues\" on Black Vinyl, \"Won\u2019t Stop\" featuring Latrice Barnett, \"Each Other\" featuring Paris Brightledge and the timeless classic \"Anytime\".\n\nIn 2006, with the help of the digital era and download sites like Traxsource and Beatport, Gregory started his own independent record label Del Records.  He released his first artist album \" I Love You More\", that got acclaimed in the Dance music industry and abroad by the likes of [[Stuart Matthewman]] ([[Sade Adu|Sade]]) and [[CeCe Rogers]] ([[Jestofunk]]).  Gregory and \"I Love You More\" were granted with a front page cover and a full page interview on the oldest UK Dance magazine [[M8 (magazine)|M8]] ([[Tilllate Magazine]]).\n\nIn 2010 Gregory has become one of the most prolific producers in the soulful side of the scene and has already produced and remixed such artists as Byron Stingily (Ten City), Susu Bobien, Keith Thompson (Raze/Break For Love), Jojo Haley, Pepper Mashay, Stephanie Cooke, Latrice Barnette, Michelle weeks, Billy Love, Bill \"The Buddah\" Dickens and Kenny Bobien amongst others. \n \nGregory has been performing as a DJ in all major events in San Francisco, and also abroad in [[Detroit]], [[Miami]], [[Los Angeles]], [[Dubai]], [[Bratislava]], [[Copenhagen]], but as with many independent producers, the worldwide economic recession and the significant increase of illegal downloads, gradually slid Gregory's career into just a hobby."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"30557015":{"pageid":30557015,"ns":0,"title":"Greg Gerber regularly DJs across the globe at events in Detroit, Berlin, Ibiza, Miami, and the UK.<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/guy-gerber-biography/  \"Guy Gerber Biography\"], [[IMO Records]] Retrieved on 1 March 2011.</ref>\n\nAt the age of 15, Gerber was a member of the Israeli Under-16 national football team but soon developed a passion for music and found himself drawn to English guitar acts like [[Joy Division]] and Irish guitar acts like [[My Bloody Valentine (band)|My Bloody Valentine]]. Consequently, his harmonic, shoe-gaze inspired sound was a style that saw Gerber record for various European electronic labels including \u2018Stoppage Time\u2019 for [[John Digweed]]\u2019s Bedrock imprint.\n\nGerber\u2019s first full length album \u2018Late Bloomers\u2019 was released on [[Sven V\u00e4th]]\u2019s Cocoon imprint in June 2007 and featured two worldwide club hits in \u2018Belly Dancing\u2019 and \u2018Sea Of Sand\u2019 which he recorded with his Israeli production friend Shlomi Aber. In addition to his productions, Guy also found time to remix [[New Order]] and [[Dominik Eulberg]] as well as setting up his own label Supplement Facts. More recently, he\u2019s remixed \u2018The L Word\u2019 by Deniz Kurtel and \u2018Hungry For The Power\u2019 by [[Azari & III]].\n\nNow living in Madrid, Supplement Facts has just celebrated its 5th anniversary with the compilation album \u2018Heartbeats\u2019. As well as releasing Gerber\u2019s own productions like \u2018Disorientation\u2019, Supplement Facts is also home to exclusive music by Lee Curtiss, David K, Michel Cleis and Varoslav feat dOP.\n\nIn Principle''' is an American [[house music]] artist and [[Record producer|producer]] born in [[Chicago]], [[Illinois]].<ref name=\"amg\">[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p13990|pure_url=yes}} allmusic ((( Jamie Principle > Biography )))<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref>  \nHe is one of the early pioneers of house music when the genre first began in Chicago during the early 1980s. Principle later began having entries on the Billboard [[Hot Dance Music/Club Play]] chart in the early 1990s,<ref>[http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/jamie-principle-biography Jamie Principle Biography]. ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 08 March 2011.</ref> including \"[[Cold World (Steve \"Silk\" Hurley and Jamie Principle song)|Cold World]]\", a #22 dance hit that is a collaboration with [[Steven Hurley|Steve \"Silk\" Hurley]], the classic \"You're All I Waited For\" on the [[Smash Records]] label, or with [[CeCe Peniston]]'s song \"[[I'm Not Over You (CeCe Peniston song)|I'm Not Over You]]\" (No.2 in [[US Dance]], No.10 in [[US R&B]]) that he would co-write.\n\nPrinciple's 1984 song \"[[Your Love (Frankie Knuckles song)|Your Love]]\" is recognised as one of the first house songs. The lyrics of the song come from a poem that Jamie Principle wrote for his girlfriend at the time, Lisa Harris. Jamie added the music and recorded the song at home on his four track recorder. A friend of his, Jose Gomez decided to record the song onto tape and give a copy to a DJ that he knew named [[Frankie Knuckles]]. Knuckles liked the song and played it regularly at a Chicago dance club called ''The Power Plant''. It continued to be a sensation in the city's underground clubs for over a year before finally being released on [[Persona records]] as a 12\" single.<ref>Fleming, J (1995), What kind of a House Party is this?</ref> Its success before an official release was entirely due to the song being played in Chicago house music clubs, then copied onto tape by fans, and eventually circulating throughout the underground scene.\n\nJamie's music continued to be released throughout the 1980s but often crediting Frankie Knuckles as the artist. Songs released included: \"Baby Wants to Ride,\" \"Cold World,\" \"Bad Boy,\" \"Rebels,\" \"Waiting on My Angel\" and \"I'm Gonna Make You Scream.\" In 1992, Principle released a dance album titled ''The Midnight Hour''.<ref name=\"Discogs\">[http://www.discogs.com/artist/Jamie+Principle Jamie Principle Discography].discogs</ref> \n\nIn 2004 Principle hit #1 on the US Dance Chart with \"Back N Da Day,\" which is an acknowledged collaboration with the, by then, house music legend, Frankie Knuckles."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2193666":{"pageid":2193666,"ns":0,"title":"Jaydee","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{distinguish2|the American hip-hop producer [[J Dilla|Jay Dee]] (or J Dilla) or the Canadian country singer [[Jaydee Bixby|Jaydee]] (Jaydee Bixby)}}\n{{for|the United States Navy ship|USS Jaydee III (SP-692)}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|image= |\n|name = JayDee\n|Background \n|birth_name = Robin Albers \n|origin = [[Netherlands]]\n|instrument =\n|genre = [[House music|House]], [[techno]]\n|occupation = [[Disc jockey|DJ]]s\n|label = \n|associated_acts =\n|website = \n|current_members =\n|past_members =\n| background=non_performing_personnel\n}}\n'''Jaydee''' (born '''Robin Albers''' in 1956) is a Dutch [[house music]] [[Record producer|producer]] and [[disc jockey|DJ]]. Jersey Street\u2019s first [[single (music)|single]], \"Nobody But My Lord\", was released on J.B.O. in 1998. It was followed by two [[album]]s, ''Step Into The Light'' and ''After The Rain'', for [[Glasgow Underground Recordings]], which were released in 2000 and 2002 respectively. The band also released singles for [[record label|labels]] including [[Yellow Productions]], Out of the Loop Records, [[Mr Bongo Records]], [[Naked Records]], [[Hed Kandi]], [[Defected Records]], and Electric Chair Records, [[PIAS Recordings]]. \n\nJersey Street began with founding producer Neil Reid, vocalist Dawn Zee and Steve Chesney (engineer/co-producer) and as other members joined the fold \u2013 primarily Matt Steele (keyboards/producer), Jasper Wilkinson (bass, saxophone and guitar)\u2013 the band's production aesthetic increasingly reflected the funk, soul and disco influences on House. Since its inception, Jersey Street has used an increasing amount of live instrumentation, including bass, guitars, horn sections and strings, as well as a looser approach to technology which made its grooves less rigid and unyielding than those of some contemporaries.{{Citation needed|date=October 2010}} The growing use of live musicians led to a string of dates as a nine-piece band, at venues including London's Cargo and Manchester's [[Band on the Wall]].\n\nDespite receiving acclaim from the [[dance music]] fraternity \u2013 and from underground music lovers in general \u2013 Jersey Street has never crossed over to a more general audience. He is one of the pioneers of [[house music]],<ref>IMO Records. [http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/jesse-saunders-biography/ \"Jesse Saunders Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]'', Retrieved on 24 February 2012.</ref> often cited as \"the originator of House music\" by critics and historians. His 1984 single, \"On & On\", co-written with [[Vince Lawrence]], was first record with a [[House music|house]] [[DJ]] as the artist that was pressed and sold to the public.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.4clubbers.net/modules.php?name=News&file=article&sid=125|accessdate=2007-11-16|title=Interviews: Marshell Jefferson| author=Mitchell, Euan|publisher=4clubbers.net |archiveurl = http://web.archive.org/web/20080101170440/http://www.4clubbers.net/modules.php?name=News&file=article&sid=125 <!-- Bot retrieved archive --> |archivedate = 2008-01-01}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.flyglobalmusic.com/fly/archives/uscanada_features/finding_jesse_-.html|title=Finding Jesse - The Discovery of Jesse Saunders as the Founder of House|work=Fly*Global Music Culture|author=Cummins, James|date=2004-10-25|accessdate=2007-11-16}}</ref>  Chicago Mayor [[Richard M. In recent years, through House music reunions, a pending book release and a live 'disc-jocumentary' - where, while DJing, he visually takes the audience through the history of House and Electro - Saunders has worked towards erasing the misconceptions associated with the genre's origins. In his early years, after studying the work of peers [[Moby]], [[Sven Vath]], [[Frankie Knuckles]], and [[Louie Vega]], Junior began to DJ and produce records himself on his own with a style rooted in the sound of the New York [[Underground music]] scene. Junior has performed in [[clubs]] and [[festivals]] throughout the [[United States]], [[Asia]], [[Australia]], and [[Europe]]. His latest album, ''Seize The Fewcha'', was praised for having \"Some of the freshest floor-fillers ever thrown on to one disc\" and Sanchez was called \"A true renaissance man whose talents are [[Dave Carlucci]]], Nitebreed [W/ Harry \u201cChoo Choo\u201d Romero], Output/Teletronik [W/ Chris Haliani], Riot Society [W/ [[Laidback Luke]] + Chris Haliani], and [[Subspecies]] [W/ [[Armand Van (born July 6, 1970)<ref name=\"allmusic\"/> - also sometimes known as '''K-Dope''' - is an American [[record producer]] and [[disc jockey]]. He is one half of the classic [[house music]] [[Masters at Work]] musical production team with [[Little Louie Vega]];  and also released the hit ''[[The Bomb! (These Sounds Fall into My Mind)]]'' as '''The Bucketheads'''.\n\nGonzalez started his [[disc jockey|DJ]] career in 1985 organizing neighborhood block parties in his home of Brooklyn, New York, with his then musical partner, Mike Delgado. Under the [[Masters at Work]] moniker, the parties became quite successful and attracted [[Todd Terry]] who later borrowed the group's name for two record releases. Terry returned the favor at a later date when he loaned Gonzalez a drum machine, which began his interest in producing beats.{{Citation needed|date=May 2012}}Kenny Dope was one of the DJ's for the group KAOS whose 1988 album \"Court's In Session\" featured production by Todd Terry."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"10087496":{"pageid":10087496,"ns":0,"title":"Kerri Chandler","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{multiple issues|\n{{Fanpov|date=January 2010}}\n{{Advert|date=August 2010}}\n}}\n\n{{Infobox musical artist\n|name = Kerri 'Kaoz' Chandler\n|image              =\n|caption         = \n|background       = group_or_band\n|alias            =\n|origin           = [[East Orange, New Jersey]] [[United States]]\n|genre            = [[Deep House]]<br>[[Garage house|Garage]]\n| label               = Madhouse Records, MadTech Records\n|Occupation(s)    =\n|years_active     = 1992&ndash;Present\n|website              = [http://www.madhouserecordsinc.com/ Official Website]\n|associated_acts = [[Dennis Ferrer]]\n[[Jerome Sydenham]]\n}}\n\n'''Kerri 'Kaoz' Chandler''', is an electronic music producer and DJ. His father was a [[DJ]] and provided Kerri with a background in the origins of [[soul music|soul]], [[disco]] and the [[New York]] Underground Sound. Accompanying his father to gigs, Kerri began playing records at the [[Rally Racquet Club]] in [[East Orange]], [[New Jersey]] at the age of thirteen.\n\nAged fourteen, he began interning in studios and producing music.<ref name=attack>{{cite web|title=Kerri Chandler - Attack Magazine|url=http://www.attackmagazine.com/features/interviews/kerri-chandler/|accessdate=9 August 2012}}</ref>  Since the (producer)|Dave Kelly]]'s reggae label of the same name) whose signings include Roy Ayers and Dennis Ferrer and more recently MadTech Records, whose roster includes No Artificial Colours, Citizen, Kashii, Waze & Odyssey and Waifs & Strays.\n\nSince the signing of his first single \"SuperLover/Get It Off\" by [[Atlantic Records]] in 1991, Kerri began producing a body of work that has helped coin past_members        =  \n}}\n\n'''K-Klass''' are a Welsh/English [[electronic music]] [[musical ensemble|group]] who originally recorded in [[Wrexham]], [[North Wales]], and are now based in [[Manchester]], [[England]]. Its original members were Andy Williams, Carl Thomas, Russ Morgan and Paul Roberts. K-Klass signed with the [[record label|label]] [[Deconstruction Records]], and later to [[Parlophone]]. Since leaving [[Parlophone]] Andy Williams and Carl Thomas have both left K-Klass leaving just Paul Roberts and Russell Morgan alongside original vocalist Bobbi Depasois as K-Klass. Roberts and Morgan run their own record label Klass Action<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/k-klass-biography/ \"K Klass Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 08 March 2011.</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4968179":{"pageid":4968179,"ns":0,"title":"The KLF","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Redirect|KLF}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = The KLF\n| image                 = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu<br />The JAMs<br />The Timelords\n| origin              = London, England\n| genre               = [[House (music)|House]], [[Techno music|techno]], [[acid house]], [[Hip hop music|hip hop]], [[alternative dance]], [[ambient house]], [[Avant-garde music|avant-garde]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.digitalinberlin.de/tag/the-klf/ |title=The KLF &#124; |publisher=Digitalinberlin.de |date=2013-12-14 |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.stewarthomesociety.org/klf.htm |title=the (un)real history of the pop avant-garde |publisher=Stewarthomesociety.org |date= |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=http://inlog.org/2011/05/20/bill-drummond-the-klf-announced-for-debate-and-the17-project-for-incubate-2011/ |title=Incubate Blog \u00bb Blog Archive \u00bb Bill Drummond (The KLF) announced for debate and The17 project for Incubate 2011 |publisher=Inlog.org |date= |accessdate=2014-01-21}}</ref>\n| years_active        = 1987\u20131992 <br><small>(Reunions: 1995 and 1997)</small>\n| label               = [[KLF Communications]], [[Arista Records|Arista]], and other international licensees\n| associated_acts     = [[The K Foundation]], [[Disco 2000]], [[Fuck the Millennium|2K]]\n| past_members        = [[Bill Drummond]]<br />[[Jimmy Cauty]]\n}}\n\n'''The KLF''' (also known as '''The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu''', '''The Timelords''' and other names) were a [[United Kingdom|British]] [[acid house]] band of the late 1980s and early 1990s.<ref>IMO Records. [http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/klf-biography/ \"The KLF Biography\"]{{dead link|date=January 2014}}, ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 29 February 2011.</ref>\n\nBeginning in 1987, [[Bill Drummond]] (alias King Boy D) and [[Jimmy Cauty]] (alias Rockman Rock) released [[hip hop music|hip hop]]-inspired and [[sampling (music)|sample]]-heavy records as '''The Justified Ancients of Mu Mu''', and on one occasion (the British number one hit [[single (music)|single]] \"[[Doctorin' the Tardis]]\") as '''The Timelords'''.  The KLF released a series of international hits on their own KLF Communications record label, and became the biggest-selling singles act in the world for 1991.<ref name=\"AMG\">Bush, J., KLF biography, ''[[Allmusic]]'' ([{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p4694/biography|pure_url=yes}} link])</ref> The duo also published a cynical book, ''[[The Manual|The Manual (How to Have a Number One the Easy Way)]]'', and worked on a road movie called ''[[The White Room (film)|The White Room]]''.\n\nFrom the outset, they adopted the philosophy espoused by esoteric novel series ''[[The Illuminatus! Trilogy]]'', gaining notoriety for various [[anarchism|anarchic]] [[Situationist International|situationist]] manifestations, including the [[vandalism|defacement]] of billboard adverts, the posting of prominent cryptic advertisements in ''[[NME]]'' magazine and the mainstream press, and highly distinctive and unusual performances on ''[[Top of the Pops]]''. Their most notorious performance was a collaboration with [[Extreme Noise Terror]] at the February 1992 [[Brit Awards|BRIT Awards]], where they fired [[machine gun]] [[Blank (cartridge)|blanks]] into the audience and dumped a dead sheep at the aftershow party. This performance announced The KLF's departure from the music business, and in May 1992 the duo [[Deletion (music industry)|deleted]] their entire back catalogue.\n\nWith The KLF's profits, Drummond and Cauty established the [[K Foundation]] and sought to subvert the [[art world]], staging an [[K Foundation art award|alternative art award]] for the worst artist of the year and [[K Foundation Burn a Million Quid|burning one million pounds sterling]]. Drummond and Cauty remained true to their word of May 1992; the KLF Communications catalogue remains deleted in the UK, but ''[[The White Room]]'' is still being pressed in the US by [[Arista Records|Arista]]. They have released a small number of new tracks since then, as the K Foundation, [[The One World Orchestra]] and most recently, in 1997, as [[Fuck the Millennium|2K]]."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"33834080":{"pageid":33834080,"ns":0,"title":"Knife Party","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Unreliable sources|date=June 2014}}\n{{Use Australian English|date=February 2013}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=October 2012}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| image               = Knife Party.jpg\n| caption             = \n| image_size          =\n| name                = Knife Party\n| background          = group_or_band\n| origin              = [[Perth, Australia]]\n| genre               = [[Electro house]], [[dubstep]], [[moombahton]], [[Drum and bass|drumstep]]\n| years_active        = {{Start date|df=yes|2011}}&ndash;present\n| label               = Earstorm, [[Big Beat Records (Atlantic Records subsidiary)|Big Beat]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Pendulum (band)|Pendulum]], [[Swedish House Mafia]], [[Steve Aoki]], [[Mistajam]]\n| website             = {{url|knifeparty.com}}\n| current_members     = [[Rob Swire]] <br />[[Gareth McGrillen]]\n|alt = Knife Party Logo\n}}\n\n'''Knife Party''' is an [[Australia]]n [[electronic dance music]] duo. June 8, 1962)<ref>''Joel Whitburn's top pop singles'' 1955-2006, pg. 475</ref> known by the stage name of '''Kristine W''', is an American [[singer-songwriter]]. She has released seven albums.  In 2004, ''[[The Advocate]]'' stated that she had helped shape the nightlife of the past decade.<ref name=\"Advocate2004\">{{cite book|last=Dave White|first=|title=The Advocate - \"Stronger than Ever\"|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=12QEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA63|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=2004-03-30|publisher=Here Publishing|pages=63\u2013}}</ref> Her first 8 singles all reached #1 on the Billboard Hot Dance Club Play charts<ref name=\"Inc.2004\">{{cite book|last=Michael Paoletta|first=|title=Billboard - Where have all the Divas gone?|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=thAEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA32|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=2004-05-01|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|pages=32\u2013}}</ref> which set a new record.<ref name=\"BillboardJune2004\">{{cite book|last=Billboard Staff|first=|title=Billboard - Kristine W Goes 8 for 8|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=jhAEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA65|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=2004-04-17|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|pages=65\u2013}}</ref> As of 2009, 14 of 15 singles had reached the top of the Billboard dance charts.<ref name=\"BillboardSept2009\">{{cite book|last=Keith Caulfield|first=|title=Billboard - Dancing Queen|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=s95YFvxALsUC&pg=PT45|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=2009-09-05|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|pages=45\u2013}}</ref>\n\nWeitz was born and raised in [[Pasco, Washington]]. Her mother was a performer.<ref name=\"Billboard.1994\">{{cite book|last=Larry Flick|first=|title=Billboard - \"Feeling Good About What She Wants\"|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=YAgEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA28|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=1994-07-23|publisher=Nielsen Business Media, Inc.|pages=28\u2013}}</ref> Weitz won the  Miss Washington (1980\u20131981) title<ref>[http://www.misstricities.org/wp-content/gallery/past-miss-tri-cities-gallery-photos/1980_kristine_weitz2.jpg Image of Kristine Weitz], misstricities.org. Retrieved 8 September 2013.</ref> and won swimsuit and talent in the Miss America Pageant.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.misswashington.org/miss%20former.html |title=MWSO Former Miss Washingtons |publisher=Misswashington.org |date= |accessdate=2014-06-06}}</ref> She then moved to Las Vegas and enrolled at the [[University of Nevada, Las Vegas]], graduated with a BA in Communications\u2013TV Production, she minored in music and marketing.\n\nWhile living in Las Vegas, she headlined a revue.<ref name=\"Advocate1996\">{{cite book|last=Barry Walters|first=|title=The Advocate - \"A New Miss Thing\"|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=OWMEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PT47|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=1996-10-15|publisher=Here Publishing|pages=47\u2013}}</ref> During a revue that featured Weitz with a number of [[drag queen]]s, she was spotted by an [[A & R]] agent who flew her to London for a recording session that resulted in the single \"Feel What You Want\".<ref name=\"Vibe1994\">{{cite book|last=Larry Flick|first=|title=Vibe - \"Kristine W The Disco Queen Rules\"|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=dywEAAAAMBAJ&pg=PA50|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=1994-12 - 1995-01|publisher=Vibe Media Group|pages=50\u2013}}</ref>\n\nAfter the release of her first single, which became very popular in overseas dance clubs, there was a bidding war by the major labels to sign Weitz.<ref name=\"Billboard.1994\"/> Weitz wrote and produced her  albums ''[[Land of the Living (album)|Land of the Living]]'' (1996) and ''[[Stronger (Kristine W album)|Stronger]]'' (2000).<ref name=\"Advocate2004\"/> The Advocate called  ''Land of the Living'' \"impressive\" and stated that she has an \"intensity\" that plays like she is a \"woman imitating a man impersonating a woman\"<ref name=\"Advocate1996\"/> while  ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'' called it \"one of the most artful song-oriented dance albums in years.\"<ref name=\"Spin1996\">{{cite book|last=Barry Walters|first=|title=SPIN - \"Review Kristine W Land of the Living\"|url=http://books.google.com/books?id=ODyv3kH8WPMC&pg=PA100|accessdate=7 June 2014|date=1996-08|publisher=SPIN Media LLC|pages=100\u2013}}</ref>  In its review of ''Stronger'' ''[[Out (magazine)|Out]]'' said that her second album lacked the \"personality\" of ''Land of the Living'' (which it cited as one of the top 10 dance albums of the decade) and was \"burdened with house beats.\"<ref name=\"Out2000\">{{cite book|last=Smith Galtney|first=|title=Out - \"Preview - Kristine W The single \"[[No Stress]]\", featuring vocals by \u00c9ric Carter, was #1 on the French SNEP Singles Chart.<ref>\"No Stress\", in French, Swiss and Belgian Singles Charts [http://lescharts.com/showitem.asp?interpret=Laurent+Wolf&titel=No+Stress&cat=s Lescharts.com] (Retrieved April 12, 2008)</ref> On October 28, 2009, [[DJ Magazine]] announced the results of their annual Top 100 DJ Poll, with [[Ultra Records]] Wolf placed at #66.<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.djmag.com/top100|title=DJ Mag's Top 100 DJ's|publisher=DJ Magazine|accessdate=2009-11-19}}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"3686228":{"pageid":3686228,"ns":0,"title":"Late Night Alumni","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist | <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject Musicians -->\n| name                = Late Night Alumni\n| image               = File:Late Night Alumni.jpg\n| caption             = Late Night Alumni at [https://www.facebook.com/nextdoorhi Nextdoor] in Honolulu, Hawaii on October 10, 2014. <br> (l-r: John Hancock, Becky Jean Williams)\n| image_size          = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[Salt Lake City]], [[Utah]], [[United States]]\n| genre               = [[House (music)|House]], [[downtempo]], [[chillout]]\n| years_active        = 2003\u2013present \n| label               = [[Hed Kandi]]<br>[[Ultra Records]]\n| associated_acts     = \n| website             = [http://www.latenightalumni.com/ www.latenightalumni.com]\n| current_members     = [[Kaskade|Ryan Raddon]]<br/>Finn Bjarnson<br/>John Hancock<br/>Becky Jean Williams\n| past_members        = \n}}\n\n'''Late Night Alumni''' is an American [[House music|house]] group composed of Becky Jean Williams, John Hancock, Finn Bjarnson and Ryan Raddon ([[Kaskade]]). They are primarily known for mixing dance music with strings and soft [[Trance music|trance]]-like vocals.<ref>IMO Records. [http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/late-night-alumni-biography/ \"Late Night Alumni Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 29 February 2011.</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4127912":{"pageid":4127912,"ns":0,"title":"Ben Watt","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use dmy dates|date=March 2011}}\n{{BLP sources|date=May 2013}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name = Ben Watt\n| image = Ben Watt by Edward Bishop.jpg\n| caption = Ben Watt by Edward Bishop\n| image_size =\n| background = solo_singer\n| birth_name = Benjamin Brian Thomas Watt\n| alias =\n| birth_place = [[Marylebone]], [[London]], [[England]]\n| birth_date = {{Birth date and age|1962|12|6|df=y}}\n| death_date =\n| origin = [[Barnes, London|Barnes]], London, England\n| instrument = [[Singing|Vocals]], [[guitar]], [[Keyboard instrument|keyboards]], [[synthesizer]], [[piano]], [[Organ (music)|organ]], [[Phonograph|turntable]], [[Programming (music)|programming]]\n| genre = [[Alternative rock]], [[new wave music|new wave]], [[techno]], [[House music|house]], [[electronica]], [[drum and bass]], [[trip hop]], [[folk rock]]\n| occupation = [[Musician]], [[singer-songwriter]], [[Disc jockey|DJ]], [[Author]], [[Record producer|producer]], [[remix]]er, [[record label]] owner, [[Presenter|radio presenter]]\n| years_active = 1981\u2013present\n| associated_acts = [[Everything but the Girl]]\n| label = [[Cherry Red Records|Cherry Red]], [[Blanco y Negro Records|Blanco y Negro]], [[Sire Records|Sire]], [[Warner Bros. Records|Warner Bros.]], [[Atlantic Records|Atlantic]], [[Virgin Records|Virgin]], Buzzin' Fly, Strange Feeling\n| publisher = [[Bloomsbury Publishing]], [[Penguin Group]]\n}}\n\n'''Benjamin Brian Thomas Watt''' (born 6 December 1962) is a British musician, singer, songwriter, author, DJ and radio presenter, best known as one half of the duo [[Everything but the Girl]].<ref name=\"Mag\" />\n\n==Early life==\nWatt was born in [[Marylebone]], London<ref>http://www.findmypast.co.uk/search/all/results?recordCount=-1&forenames=Benjamin&_includeForenamesVariants=on&surname=Watt&_includeSurnameVariants=on&fromYear=1962&toYear=1962&region=&county=&mothersMaidenName=&_useMothersMaidenNameAsSurname=on&sortOrder=RK%3Atrue&_performExactSearch=on&event=B&recordType=ALL&route=</ref> and grew up in [[Barnes, London|Barnes]], the son of Scottish jazz musician [[Tommy Watt]] and showbusiness writer [[Romany Bain]],<ref>http://benwatt.com/work/books/romany-and-tom |accessdate=25 April 2014</ref> and has four half brothers and sisters.<ref name=\"Mag\">{{cite web|title=INTERVIEW: BEN WATT|url=http://www.m-magazine.co.uk/interviews/interview-ben-watt/|work=M Magazine|publisher=PRS for Music|accessdate=13 June 2013|date=13 June 2013}}</ref> He is the youngest of the family.<ref>{{cite news|title=Girl trouble|url=http://www.theguardian.com/theobserver/1999/sep/12/life1.lifemagazine1|accessdate=27 April 2014|newspaper=The Observer|date=12 September 1999}}</ref>\n\n==Recording artist==\n{{main|Everything but the Girl}}\nWatt began recording in 1981 on the indie label [[Cherry Red Records|Cherry Red]]. His first single 'Cant' was produced by folk-maverick [[Kevin Coyne]]. His second release, 1982's 5-track EP 'Summer into Winter' featured [[Robert Wyatt]] on backing vocals and piano.<ref>{{cite web|title=Ben Watt with Robert Wyatt - Summer into Winter|url=http://www.discogs.com/Ben-Watt-Summer-Into-Winter/release/970741|website=Discogs}}</ref> His debut album ''[[North Marine Drive]]'' was released in 1983 and reached Number 1 on UK Indie Charts.<ref>{{cite web|title=North Marine Drive (1983)|url=http://www.popmatters.com/post/171476-ben-watt-north-marine-drive-198|website=Pop Matters}}</ref> He then took a fork in the road and joined forces with vocalist [[Tracey Thorn]], with whom he wrote and recorded with for 18 years\u2014together they created nine studio albums as Everything but the Girl (EBTG) after signing to Blanco Y Negro through [[Warner Bros.|Warners]] in 1984, and then [[Virgin records|Virgin]] in 1995. EBTG have received eight gold, and one platinum album BPI Certifications in the UK, and one gold album RIAA Certification in the US.<ref>{{cite web|title=Everything But The Girl Awards|url=http://www.mfyi.com/e/everythingbutthegirlawards.html|website=mfyi.com|accessdate=2 October 2014}}</ref> The song \"[[Missing (Everything but the Girl song)|Missing]]\" reached number two on the US [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]] in 1995.\n\nFollowing EBTG's self-imposed hiatus in 2000, Watt immersed himself in the world of underground electronic music both as a DJ and recording artist/producer. His recorded output during this period includes club tracks such as \"Lone Cat (Holding On)\", \"A Stronger Man\" featuring Sananda Maitreya (formerly known as [[Terence Trent D'Arby]]), the \"Outspoken EP Part 1\" including \"Pop A Cap in Yo' Ass\" featuring [[Estelle (musician)|Estelle]], \"Just a Blip\" and \"Guinea Pig\".<ref>{{cite web|title=Ben Watt Discography at Discogs|url=http://www.discogs.com/artist/19004-Ben-Watt|website=Discogs|accessdate=27 September 2014}}</ref>\n\nIn 2014 Watt returned to his folk-jazz roots and released his first solo album since 1983, ''Hendra'', on 14 April 2014, the content of which was recorded with a new band including [[Bernard Butler]], formerly of the band [[Suede (band)|Suede]]\u2014Watt explained that he knew that Butler would be the \"perfect counterpoint to bring some darkness to the light.\"<ref name=\"The\">{{cite web|title=WATCH: Ben Watt & Bernard Butler - Hendra|url=http://thequietus.com/articles/14542-ben-watt-hendra-bernard-butler-tour|work=The Quietus|publisher=The Quietus|accessdate=18 April 2014|author=Laurie Tuffrey|date=19 February 2014}}</ref> Watt also worked with Berlin-based producer [[Ewan Pearson]] and [[David Gilmour]] of [[Pink Floyd]]. The album is released on a new record label, titled \"Unmade Road\", founded by Watt in 2014.<ref>{{cite web|title=Unmade Road|url=http://www.residentadvisor.net/record-label.aspx?id=11087|work=Resident Advisor|publisher=Resident Advisor Ltd|accessdate=19 April 2014|year=2014}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|title=Hendra review \u2013 Ben Watt's first solo album in 30 years|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2014/apr/13/ben-watt-hendra-review|accessdate=19 April 2014|newspaper=The Guardian|date=13 April 2014|author=Molloy Woodcraft}}</ref> Watt completed over sixty live shows in support of 'Hendra' including tours of UK, North America, Japan and Australia. The album won the 'Best 'Difficult' Second Album' category at the AIM Independent Music Awards 2014.<ref>{{cite web|title=AIM Independent Music Awards 2014|url=http://www.musicindie.com/awards|website=Association of Independent Music|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref> It was included at No 27 in Uncut's Top 75 Albums of 2014.<ref>{{cite web|title=Uncut Top 75 Albums of 2014|url=http://www.albumoftheyear.org/list/306-uncuts-top-75-albums-of-2014/}}</ref> Rolling Stone (Germany) made it their No 2 best album of 2014.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.facebook.com/benwattmusic/photos/a.564759563592741.1073741828.560032020732162/753380468063982/}}</ref> Japan's Music Magazine made it their No 3 best album of 2014.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.facebook.com/benwattmusic/photos/pb.560032020732162.-2207520000.1427453402./755072817894747}}</ref>\n\n==Writer==\nWatt's first memoir ''[[Patient (memoir)|Patient]]'' (Penguin, 1996) describes his battle dealing with [[Churg-Strauss syndrome]], a rare life-threatening [[auto-immune disease]] with which he was diagnosed in 1992. The book was listed as a ''New York Times'' Notable Book of the Year, a ''Sunday Times'' Book Of The Year chosen by [[William Boyd (writer)|William Boyd]] and ''Village Voice'' Literary Supplement Favorite Book of the Year, and was also a finalist for the Esquire-Waterstones Best Non-Fiction Award in the UK.<ref>{{cite web|title=Bloomsbury - Ben Watt|url=http://www.bloomsbury.com/author/ben-watt|website=Bloomsbury Publishing|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref>\n\nHis second memoir, ''Romany and Tom'' - a portrait of his parents' lives and marriage - was published by Bloomsbury in February 2014.<ref>http://www.bloomsbury.com/uk/romany-and-tom-9781408845271/</ref> In September 2014 it was long-listed for the [[Samuel Johnson Prize]] 2014.<ref>{{cite web|title=Musician Ben Watt makes Samuel Johnson non-fiction list|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/entertainment-arts-29014170|website=BBC News Entertainment and Arts|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref>\n\n==DJ, Remixer, Label Owner==\n\n===Lazy Dog (1998\u20132003)===\nIn 1998 Watt established the London [[deep house]] Sunday club and compilation series \"Lazy Dog\" with Jay Hannan. The club was hosted twice-monthly at the [[Notting Hill Arts Club]] in west London - and later every two months at The End in central London - and attracted a cult following. At the same time Watt moved away from EBTG's mainstream eclecticism and into club-oriented dance music production, producing a string of dance remixes for [[Sade Adu|Sade]], [[Sunshine Anderson]], [[Zero 7]], [[Maxwell (musician)|Maxwell]], [[Meshell Ndegeocello]] and [[Sandy Rivera]]. Lazy Dog ended on 16 May 2003 with a farewell closing party at the club's second home [[The End (club)|The End]] in central London. Two mix compilations - ''Lazy Dog Vol. 1'' <ref>{{cite web|title=Various - Lazy Dog Vol 1|url=http://www.discogs.com/Various-Lazy-Dog/release/681526|website=Discogs}}</ref> and ''Lazy Dog Vol. 2'' <ref>{{cite web|title=Various - Lazy Dog Vol 2|url=http://www.discogs.com/Various-Lazy-Dog-Volume-2/release/59970|website=Discogs|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref> were released by Virgin Records in 2000 and 2001 respectively.\n\n===Neighbourhood and Cherry Jam (2002\u201305)===\nFor three years between 2002 and 2005, Watt was a co-owner/founder of the West London nightclubs 'Neighbourhood' and 'Cherry Jam'.<ref>{{cite web|title=Mega Watt|url=http://www.standard.co.uk/showbiz/mega-watt-7235824.html|website=www.standard.co.uk|accessdate=2 October 2014}}</ref> Under Watt's creative direction Cherry Jam hosted underground club nights, art exhibitions, the inaugural events for the long-running [[spoken word]] night 'Book Slam'<ref>{{cite web|title=Book Slam {{!}} London's best literary night club|url=http://www.bookslam.com|website=www.bookslam.com|accessdate=2 October 2014}}</ref> and [[The Libertines]]' official debut show.<ref>{{cite web|title=The Libertines: Cherry Jam review|url=http://www.rockfeedback.com/magazine/detail/the-libertines-the-beatings-london-cherry-jam-21-02-02|website=www.rockfeedback.com}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|title=NME Reviews|url=http://www.nme.com/reviews/6142|website=www.nme.com|accessdate=2 October 2014}}</ref> At Neighbourhood, Watt brought in artists such as [[Groove Armada]] and many international DJs to perform at his own in-house club nights. Watt also hosted the 25th Anniversary of the [[Rough Trade Records]] music label<ref>{{cite web|title=Libertines/Fiery Furnaces, Neighbourhood, London|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2003/oct/17/popandrock.libertines|website=www.guadian.co.uk|accessdate=2 October 2014}}</ref> and the inaugural 'House Music Awards' ceremony.<ref name=\"House Music Awards 2004 Winners\">{{cite web|title=House Music Awards 2004 Winners|url=http://dancemusic.about.com/od/conference/a/HMA2K4Winner.htm|website=About Entertainment|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref>\n\n===Buzzin' Fly (2003\u20132013)===\nIn April 2003, Watt launched his own independent [[deep house]] and techno record label Buzzin' Fly (named after the [[Tim Buckley]] song). The label proceeded to foster the careers of young and emerging producers/DJs such as Justin Martin,<ref>{{cite web|title=Justin Martin - The Water Song [Buzzin' Fly, 2006]|url=http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=o53zqrgTS6c|work=YouTube|publisher=Google, Inc|accessdate=21 May 2013|author=DeepDownUR2|format=Audio upload|date=15 September 2011}}</ref> Mademoiselle Caro & Franck Garcia,<ref name=\"Rob\">{{cite web|title=A Fond Farewell: Buzzin' Fly|url=http://www.clashmusic.com/features/a-fond-farewell-buzzin-fly|work=Clash|publisher=Clash|accessdate=21 May 2013|author=Robin Murray|date=24 April 2013}}</ref> and Rodamaal.<ref>{{cite web|title=Rodamaal/Lephtee - Buzzin' Fly Volume III - The Special Remixes EP|url=http://www.residentadvisor.net/review-view.aspx?id=3911|work=Resident Advisor|publisher=Resident Advisor Ltd|accessdate=21 May 2013|author=Mohson Iqbal|date=31 July 2006}}</ref> The label hosted Watt's own club productions as well as work from remixers such as Ame, Radio Slave, [[Charles Webster (musician)|Charles Webster]] and [[John Tejada]].\n\nBuzzin' Fly won Best Breakthrough Label at the House Music Awards in 2004,<ref name=\"House Music Awards 2004 Winners\"/> and was awarded the Runner-Up Best British Label by the [[DJ Magazine]] Awards in both 2007 and 2008.<ref>{{cite web|title=Spotify Playlist: Buzzin' Fly Records Special From Ben Watt|url=http://thequietus.com/articles/03841-everything-but-the-girl-ben-watt-spotify-playlist|work=The Quietus|publisher=TheQuietus.com|accessdate=21 May 2013|date=5 March 2010}}</ref> Watt announced the partial closure of the label in an official statement in April 2013.<ref name=allgoodthings>{{cite web|title=All Good Things ...|url=http://www.buzzinfly.com/article.php?a=all-good-things-...|website=Buzzin' Fly Records|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref>\n\n===Strange Feeling Records (2007\u2013)===\nBuilding upon the foundation of Buzzin' Fly, Watt launched Strange Feeling Records in 2007 as a sister label that would release alternative/indie music. The critically acclaimed Copenhagen band [[Figurines]] and the Hungarian trio [[The Unbending Trees]] were early signings of Strange Feeling. In 2010 the label globally released and distributed the third solo album ''[[Love and Its Opposite]]'' by Watt's wife [[Tracey Thorn]] on 17 May 2010\u2014the album was the label's fifth release.<ref>{{cite web|title=Tracey Thorn Love and Its Opposite Review|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/music/reviews/d8zb|work=BBC Music|publisher=BBC|accessdate=21 May 2013|author=Wendy Roby|date=11 May 2010}}</ref> This was followed by her alternative Christmas album, Tinsel and Lights, in 2012.<ref>{{cite web|title=Tracey Thorn: Tinsel and Lights - review by Alexis Petridis|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2012/oct/25/tracey-thorn-tinsel-and-lights-review|website=The Guardian}}</ref> In the announcement of Buzzin Fly's closure, the press release went on to say that Strange Feeling Records would remain \"quietly active\" for future Tracey Thorn releases.<ref name=allgoodthings/>\n\n==Radio presenter==\nIn 2006 Watt launched an online radio show that soon moved to the Galaxy Network <ref>{{cite web|title=The Galaxy Network |url=http://www.billboard.com/biz/tag/The%20Galaxy%20Network?f%5B0%5D=im_opencalais_socialtags_tags%3A295575|website=Billboard|accessdate=22 September 2014}}</ref> and then Kiss. In 2010 he moved to the [[BBC Radio 6 Music]]'s flagship electronic radio show the 6Mix.<ref>{{cite web|title=BBC Radio 6 Music - 6 Mix, Ben Watt|url=http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/b00vsv7p|website=BBC}}</ref>\n\n==Personal life==\nWatt lives with his spouse and creative partner Thorn in [[Hampstead]], north London. They met at Hull University in 1981 and after 27 years together, they married in 2008 at the Chelsea Registry Office. Their twin daughters Jean and Alfie were born in 1998, and their son Blake was born in 2001.<ref>{{cite news|title=Girl trouble|url=http://www.guardian.co.uk/theobserver/1999/sep/12/life1.lifemagazine1|accessdate=13 June 2013|newspaper=The Guardian|date=12 September 1999}}</ref>\n\n==Discography==\n\n===Albums===\n* ''[[North Marine Drive]]'' (1983, [[Cherry Red Records|Cherry Red]])\n* ''[[Hendra (Ben Watt album)|Hendra]]'' (2014, Unmade Road dist. by [[Caroline International]]) UK #46\n\n===Singles and EPs===\n* \"Cant\" (June 1981, Cherry Red)\n* ''Summer Into Winter EP'' with [[Robert Wyatt]] (March 1982, Cherry Red)\n* \"Some Things Don't Matter\" (February 1983, Cherry Red)\n* \"Lone Cat (Holding On)\" (April 2003, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Buzzin' Fly Vol 1 EP\" includes \"A Stronger Man\" with [[Sananda Maitreya]] (January 2004, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Outspoken Part 1\" includes \"Pop a Cap in Yo' Ass\" with Estelle and \"Attack, Attack, Attack\" with Baby Blak (January 2005, Buzzin' Fly)\n* ''Buzzin' Fly Vol 2 EP'' includes \"Lone Cat (Holding On)\" (Justin Martin Remix) and \"Pop a Cap in Yo Ass\" (Dubstrumental) by Ben Watt with Estelle (April 2005, Buzzin' Fly)\n* ''We Are Silver EP'' includes \"Old Soul\" with Baby Blak, and \"Lone Cat\" ([[Dennis Ferrer]] & Steve Martinez Special Re-Rub) (April 2007, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Buzzin' Fly Vol 4 EP\" includes \"Just a Blip\" (June 2007, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Guinea Pig\" (October 2008, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Bright Star\" by Stimming, Ben Watt & Julia Biel (Feb 2010, Buzzin' Fly)\n* \"Forget\" (includes acoustic version of \"The Levels\" recorded with [[David Gilmour]]). From left to right: Earl 16, Djum Djum, Neil Barnes, Sebastien Beresford, Cheshire Cat and Adam Wren.\n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[London]], England\n| genre               = [[Progressive house]]\n| years_active        = 1989&ndash;2002, 2010&ndash;present\n| label               = [[Infectious Records|Infectious Music]] <small>(present)</small><br />Outer Rhythm / [[Rhythm King Records|Rhythm King]], Hard Hands / [[Chrysalis Music]], [[Columbia Records|Columbia]] / [[Sony Music Entertainment|SME Records]] <small>(former)</small>\n| associated_acts     = [[Earl Sixteen]], [[John Lydon]], [[Roots Manuva]], [[Afrika Bambaataa]]\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.leftfieldmusic.com/}}\n| current_members     = Neil Barnes\n| past_members        = Paul Daley\n|       \n}}\n\n'''Leftfield''' is a [[United Kingdom|British]] [[electronic music|electronic]] project formed in 1989 in [[London]], England. From 1989 to 2002, Leftfield was a [[duet (music)|duo]] of [[musician|artists]] and [[record producer]]s that consisted of Neil Barnes and Paul Daley (formerly of [[The Rivals (band)|the Rivals]], [[A Man Called Adam]] and the [[Brand New Heavies]]). In January 2010, Barnes resurrected Leftfield and having toured the world for a couple of years has finished writing new material for a third album entitled ''Alternative Light Source''. Daley has declined to be involved and is focusing upon his solo career.\n\nThe duo were hugely influential in the evolution of electronic music in the 1990s with [[Mixmag]] describing them as \"the single most influential production team working in British dance music\".<ref name=\"mixmagfeb1995\">{{cite journal | author=Frank Tope| title=Burn Bassbins Burn | journal=Mixmag | date=February 1995 | pages=46\u201350 | issue=45 | volume=2 }}</ref> As with many of their contemporaries such as [[the Chemical Brothers]], Leftfield were notable for their use of guest vocalists in their electronic music. Among the more prominent were [[Toni Halliday]] on \"[[Original (Leftfield song)|Original]]\", [[Johnny Rotten]] on \"[[Open Up (Leftfield song)|Open Up]]\", [[Djum Djum]] on \"[[Afro-Left]]\", and [[Earl 16]] and [[Cheshire Cat (musician)|Cheshire Cat]] on \"[[Release the Pressure]]\". The term [[progressive house]] was coined to define their style, a fusion of [[house music|house]] with [[Dub music|dub]] and [[reggae]].<ref name=\"melodymaker1992\">{{cite journal | title=RELEASE THE PRESSURE! | journal=Melody Maker | date=1992-12-05 }}</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"17688601":{"pageid":17688601,"ns":0,"title":"Le Knight Club","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"#REDIRECT [[Guy-Manuel de Homem-Christo]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"14832590":{"pageid":14832590,"ns":0,"title":"Lenny Fontana","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP sources|date=April 2015}}\n{{Infobox musical artist\n| name                = Lenny Fontana\n| image_size          = <!-- Only for images narrower than 220 pixels -->\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Leonard Fontana\n| alias               = Powerhouse\n| birth_place         = [[New York City]], [[United States]] \n| instrument          = [[Drum machine]]<br>[[Synthesizer]]<br>[[Electronic keyboard]]<br>[[Music sequencer|Sequencer]]\n| genre               = [[House Music|House]], [[Vocal House|House]]\n| occupation          = [[Disc Jockey|DJ]], [[Record producer|producer]], [[remixer]]\n| years_active        = 1985\u2013present\n| label               = Karmic Power Records, FFRR,<br>[[Strictly Rhythm]]\n| associated_acts     = [[Duane Harden]]\n| website             = [http://www.lennyfontana.com www.lennyfontana.com]\n}}\n\n'''Lenny Fontana''' is an [[United States|American]] [[house music]] [[Disc jockey|DJ]] from [[New York City]].\n\nFontana first began deejaying professionally in the mid-1980s, playing at clubs such as Studio 54 and Better Days.<ref>[http://www.inthemix.com.au/events/reviews/9380/Lenny_Fontana_Ambar_Perth_210303 Performance Review], In The Mix, March 21, 2003. Accessed December 21, 2007.</ref> His first major exposure was with the track \"A Mystical Journey\", which hit #30 on the [[United States|US]] ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Songs|Hot Dance Club/Play]] [[record chart|chart]] in 1996.<ref>[{{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p224578|pure_url=yes}} Chart Positions], Allmusic.com</ref> He won international recognition as part of the production team for [[Powerhouse (1999 band)|Powerhouse]], who scored a #1 dance hit in the US with \"What You Need\"; the song also hit #13 on the [[UK Singles Chart]].<ref>[http://www.everyhit.com/searchsec.php Search for \"Powerhouse\"] at Everyhit.com on December 21, 2007.</ref> In 2000, he returned to the UK chart with \"Chocolate Sensation\" (featuring [[DJ Shorty]]), peaking at #39.<ref>[http://www.everyhit.com/searchsec.php Search for \"Lenny Fontana\"] at Everyhit.com on December 21, 2007.</ref> He continues to make international appearances regularly.\n\nHis 2008 single \"Wait 4 U\" (a collaboration with UK producer [[Ridney]] and vocalist Larisa) was released through the Ministry of Sound (Germany) in June that year. The track had already been used on Germany's Next Top Model 2008,<ref>[http://www.ministryofsound.de/core/germanys_next_top_modep_1.php Ministry of Sound Germany<!-- Bot generated title -->]</ref> and Ministry's.<ref>[http://www.ministryofsound.de/core/produkt_details.php?mos_id=247&prod_identity=P7a5G53G7hMsTvmiNFfZMqRfZ&identity=P7a5G53G7hMsTvmiNFfZMqRfZ&artist=&title=&product_cat=CD%20Compilation&product_name=Club%20Files%20Vol.%204 Club Files 4 - Ministry of Sound]</ref>\n\n2013 Lenny Fontana founded the label Karmic Power Record\n\nLenny Fontana's classic 90s house anthem Chocolate Sensation is back for 2015 with a brand new remix. Originally signed by Pete Tong to his FFRR imprint, the track now returns on Cr2/Karmic Power Records with this huge remix from Paul Woolford aka Special Request."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2179791":{"pageid":2179791,"ns":0,"title":"Lil Louis","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{BLP sources|date=November 2010}}\n'''Lil Louis''' is the stage name used by [[Chicago]]-born [[house music|house-music]] [[Record producer|producer]] and [[disc jockey|DJ]] '''Marvin Burns'''.<ref name=\"Larkin\">Larkin, Colin (1999) ''The Virgin Encyclopedia of Dance Music'', Virgin Books, ISBN 0-7535-0252-6, p. 198</ref>  He scored a number of [[hit record|hits]] on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Music/Club Play]] [[record chart|chart]] in the 1980s and 1990s, three of which hit [[chart-topper|#1]].<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/lil-louis-biography/  \"Lil Louis Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 08 March 2011.</ref>\n\nHis best known [[song]], \"[[French Kiss (song)|French Kiss]],\" featured [[human voice|vocals]] by [[Shawn Christopher]] and spent two weeks at #1 on the dance chart in 1989. The track features a several-minutes-long breakdown in which the music gradually slowed down in [[tempo]] to a stop.  Even with its sensual sound, it crossed over to some [[pop music|pop]] [[radio station]]s and climbed to #50 on the [[Billboard Hot 100|''Billboard'' Hot 100]]. It was a big success throughout [[Europe]] reaching #2 in the [[UK Singles Chart]]<ref name=\"Larkin\" /> and in [[Germany]], and number one in the Netherlands.\n\nThe video was directed by Marek Budzynski\n\n[[Laurent Garnier]]'s 1997 12\" [[single (music)|single]] \"Flashback\" contained a remix made by Lil Louis called \"Lil Louis Civilized Instrumental Painting.\"\n\nBritish Drum 'n' Bass producers [[Ed Rush]] & [[Optical (artist)|Optical]] remixed the track \"[[French Kiss (song)|French Kiss]]\".\n\nIn 2000, fellow producer [[Josh Wink]] released \"How's Your Evening So Far?\"\u2014credited to Wink vs. Lil Louis\u2014a track that heavily sampled \"French Kiss.\" The song peaked at #3 on the dance chart.  The song was also [[sampling (music)|sampled]] in 2000 by female [[hip hop music|hip hop]] emcee [[Lil' Kim]] on the track \"Custom Made (Give It To You),\" which was featured on ''[[The Notorious KIM]]''.\n\nLouis also released albums under the names Li'l Louis & the World and Li'l Louis & the Party.\n\nIn the track \"Teachers\" from the ''[[Homework (Daft Punk album)|Homework]]'' album by [[Daft Punk]], Lil' Louis is one of the many [[musician]]s mentioned.\nIn November 2012, accusations against Louis from Australian promoters in regards to his tour where he did not make it to Australia and perform and he kept the performance fee [http://www.whoislillouis.com/]. The blog/site became viral in the electronic music scene with coverage from all major newspapers and online magazines. \nIn 2013, [[John Legend]] released the song \"Made to Love\", which features a prominent sample of the Lil' Louis song \"Video Clash\",<ref>{{cite web|title=John Legend's Made to Love sample of Lil' Louis's The Original Video Clash|url=http://www.whosampled.com/sample/213331/John-Legend-Made-to-Love-Lil'-Louis-The-Original-Video-Clash/|publisher=Whosampled|accessdate=29 August 2013}}</ref> on [[Kanye West]]'s [[GOOD Music|G.O.O.D. Music]] label.\n\nOn 24 January 2015, Louis suffered sound-induced [[hearing loss]] in his left ear during a [[soundcheck]] in [[Manchester,     = Little Louie Vega\n| image               = Louie Vega.jpg\n| caption             = \"Little\" Louie Vega at club Air, Tokyo - April 29, 2014. Bringing his NYC residency party \"Dance Ritual\" abroad.\n| image_size          =\n| background          = non_vocal_instrumentalist\n| birth_name          = Luis Fernando Vager\n| alias               =\n| birth_date          = {{Birth date and age|mf=y|1965|6|12}}\n| birth_place         = [[The Bronx, New York|The Bronx]], [[New York]], [[United States]]\n| death_date          =\n| origin              =\n| instrument          =\n| genre               = [[House music|House]], [[Club music|Club]], [[Latin music|Latin]]\n| occupation          = [[DJ]], [[Music producer|Producer]], [[Remixer]]\n| years_active        =\n| label               = [[Vega Records]], [[Defected Records]]\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             = {{URL|http://www.vegarecords.net}}\n| current_members     =\n| past_members        =\n| notable_instruments =\n}}\n\n'''Luis Fernando Vega''' (born June 12, 1965), better known as '''\"Little\" Louie Vega''', is an American musician of [[Puerto Ricans in the United States|Puerto Rican]] ancestry. He is one half of the [[Masters At Work]] musical production team.<ref>{{cite web|url={{Allmusic|class=artist|id=p134431|pure_url=yes}}|title=Biography: \"Little\" Louie Vega|last=Potts|first=Diana|publisher=[[Allmusic]]|accessdate=23 May 2010}}</ref>  He was born to a musician family, as his father, Luis Vager, was a [[jazz music|jazz]] [[saxophone|saxophonist]], and his uncle was singer [[H\u00e9ctor Lavoe]] of the [[Fania All-Stars]], and he started his [[DJ]] career spinning records at the age of 13.<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/louie-vega-biography/  \"Little Louie Vega Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 08 March 2011.</ref>\n\nBy 1985, Louie who is cousin to Eric Vega, popular event creator and promoter in New York City began playing house and block parties in his local [[Bronx]] neighborhood of [[New York]], as well as engineering and mixing. ([[Erasure]]'s ''[[The Two Ring Circus]]'' features his earliest dabblings in the studio.)  His first [[nightclub]] residency was at the Devil's Nest, in the Bronx, and later he moved to Roseland, [[Studio 54]] and the Palladium in [[Manhattan]].  During the 1990s, Vega was playing at one of the most influential nightclubs for [[house music]], [[The Sound Factory Bar]]. By the mid 1990s, the Masters At Work team had Vega spending less time behind the turntables and more time in the studio as part of the team's [[remix]]ers."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2194894":{"pageid":2194894,"ns":0,"title":"Livin' Joy","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Livin' Joy\n| image                 = \n| caption            = \n| image_size            = \n| background          = group_or_band\n| alias               = \n| origin              = [[Italy]]\n| genre               = [[Electronic dance music]] (EDM)<br>[[Eurodance]], [[Italo house]], [[dance-pop]]\n| years_active        = 1994\u20131999\n| label               = \n| associated_acts     = \n| website                 = \n| current_members     =\n| past_members        = Paolo Visnadi<br>Gianni Visnadi<br>Tameka Starr <small>(1996-1999)<br>[[Janice Robinson]] <small>(1994-1996)</small>\n| notable_instruments = \n}}\n'''Livin' Joy''' were an [[Italy|Italian]] eurodance group who released two successful dance [[hit record|hits]] during the mid-1990s, \"[[Dreamer (Livin' Joy song)|Dreamer]]\" and \"[[Don't Stop Movin' (Livin' Joy song)|Don't Stop Movin']]\". RedFoo and Sky Blu grew up in the affluent [[Los Angeles]] neighborhood [[Pacific Palisades, Los Angeles|Pacific Palisades]], where they formed the group LMFAO in 2006 and later became part of the electro house scene. LMFAO started building a local buzz through their shows and radio play. In 2010, they were featured on [[David Guetta]]'s smash hit \"[[Gettin' Over You]]\", which charted all over Europe and the U.S., including reaching number one in the [[UK Singles Chart]].\n\nLMFAO are best remembered for their song \"[[Party Rock Anthem]]\", which reached #1 in the [[United Kingdom]], [[Australia]], [[Belgium]], [[Brazil]], [[Canada]], [[Denmark]], [[France]], [[Germany]], [[Ireland]], [[New Zealand]], [[Switzerland]], and the [[United States]]. The song also reached the top five in [[Italy]] and [[Norway]]. Worldwide, \"Party Rock Anthem\" was the third best-selling digital single of 2011 with sales of 9.7 million copies; it is also their biggest throughout their career. \"Shuffling\" is a reference to a [[Melbourne shuffle|dance style]] from Melbourne, Australia, hence the song's popularity in the Australian charts. sources|date=October 2014}}\n{{fanpov|date=October 2014}}\n}}\n\n{{EngvarB|date=August 2014}}\n{{Use dmy dates|date=August 2014}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- For individuals; see Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name                = Louis La Roche\n| image               = \n| alt                 =\n| caption             =\n| image_size          =\n| background          = non_performing_personnel\n| birth_name          = Brett Ewels\n| alias               = Louis La Roche\n| birth_date          = {{birth-date and age|df=yes|15 September 1990}}\n| birth_place         =\n| origin              = [[Norwich]], United Kingdom\n| instrument          =\n| genre               = French house, nu-disco, funk\n| occupations          = Songwriter, producer, Remixer, DJ\n| years_active        = 2008 \u2013 Present\n| label               = Ever After Records, Spinnin' Records, Om Records, Nurvous Records,\n| associated_acts     =\n| website             = {{URL|http://louislaroche.com/}}\n| notable_instruments =\n}}\n\n'''Brett Ewels''' (born 15 September 1990), best known by his stage name '''Louis La Roche''', is a [[French house]]/[[nu-disco]]/[[funk]] producer, remixer and DJ from [[Norwich]], UK.<ref>IMO Records. http://www.imorecords.co.uk/house-2/house-artists/louis-la-roche-biography/  \"Louis La Roche Biography\"], ''[[IMO Records]]' Retrieved on 8 March 2011.</ref>\n\nLouis La Roche sprung to prominence in 2008 with his [[Michael Jackson]] sampled debut track '''Love''' (which was originally mistaken for [[Daft Punk]]) and featured on an unofficial five-track EP entitled ''''''The Peach EP'''''' (2008). The track quickly made an impact across online blogs and led to recognition via an article by the British newspaper [[The Guardian]].<ref>The Guardian. http://www.theguardian.com/music/2010/jan/04/new-band-louis-la-roche  \"Louis La Roche - New Band Of The Day\"], ''[[The Guardian]]' Retrieved on 21 November 2014.</ref> From there, Louis went on to form his own record label ''''''Ever After Records'''''', on which he released the EP's ''''''Me & Her'''''' (2009), ''''''Super Soaker'''''' (2010) and ''''''Number One'''''' (2011), a collaboration with German producer [[Patrick Alavi]]. He followed this with the single ''''''My Turn'''''', which featured guest vocals by [[Yann Destal]] of [[Modjo]].\n\nAt the end of 2011, Louis' next single ''''''Gimme Gimme/The Wall'''''' topped the [[Beatport]] Electronica chart, which was shortly followed by the neighbouring single ''''''Untrue/Touch Wood''''''. The track featured a guest appearance from upcoming UK rapper ''Ad-Apt'' and contains vocals by Louis himself. Both singles had accompanying videos which were featured on YouTube.\n\nIn 2013, Louis released the five-track EP ''''''Composure'''''' on Ever After Records, shortly followed by the double A-side single ''''''Kaboom/Funk Trunk Skunk'''''' on [[Om Records]]. This single had accompanying music videos which were exclusively featured on [[Vevo]].\n\nDuring 2014, Louis released the single ''''''Offline'''''' featuring J Paul Getto & Lizzie Curious on Nurvous Records. This was then followed up with a late 80's inspired EP entitled ''''''Dusty Cassette'''''' on Ever After Records.<ref>Bandcamp. https://iamlouislaroche.bandcamp.com/album/dusty-cassette-ep  \"Louis La Roche - Dusty Cassette EP\", ''[[Bandcamp]] Retrieved on 19 November 2014.</ref>\n\nIn addition to his own material, Louis has created a string of official remixes for artists such as [[Basement Jaxx]], [[Fred Falke]], [[Spiller]], [[Aeroplane (musician)|Aeroplane]], Mike Mago, [[Don Diablo]], [[VV Brown]], [[Del Marquis]] (of the [[Scissor Sisters]]), [[:fr:Teenage Bad Girl|Teenage Bad Girl]], [[Mercury Music Prize]] winner [[Speech Debelle]] and [[The Supermen Lovers]]. Unofficial remixes include the likes of [[Michael Jackson]], [[Calvin Harris]], [[Miley Cyrus]], [[Riva Starr]] & [[Fatboy Slim]], Burial, [[Kate Bush]] and [[Gorillaz]].\n\nHis tracks have appeared on compilations by [[Ministry of Sound]], [[Modular Recordings|Modular]], Neon, [[Hed Kandi]], [[Defected Records|Defected]] and Annie Mac Presents. Louis La Roche has received radio airplay from DJs such as [[Pete Tong]],<ref>Pete Tong Radio 1. http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/b04ybprl \"Pete Tong Radio 1 show 23/01/15\", [[BBC Radio 1]] Retrieved on 23 January 2015.</ref> [[Annie Mac]], [[Zane Lowe]], [[Alex Metric]], [[MistaJam]], [[Kissy Sellout]], [[Benji B]], [[Huw Stephens]],<ref>Huw Stephens Radio 1. http://www.bbc.co.uk/programmes/b04xnnyf \"Huw Stephens Radio 1 show 21/01/15\", [[BBC Radio 1]] Retrieved on 22 January 2015.</ref> and Jaymo & Andy George. He has had exclusives mixes on [[Kiss (UK radio station)|Kiss FM]] and Australian radio station [[Triple J]]. In 2012 Louis hosted an hour-long show for [[BBC Radio Norfolk]] as part of the BBC Introducing programme.\n\nIn addition to radio, Louis has also written music for television, being featured in the [[Channel 4]] series [[Skins (TV series)|''Skins'']] as well as composing the theme song for Canada's [[MuchMusic Video Awards]]. Louis La Roche was featured as [[The Guardian]] Music's first [http://www.theguardian.com/music/2010/jan/04/new-band-louis-la-roche 'New Band of The Day' (no. 696)] for 2010. Louis was featured in the UK music magazine '''''Future Music''''' (published on 9 May 2012) and [http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdRCSGsLJkk recorded a video] interview in the MofoHifi studio in London, where he discusses working with [[FL Studio]], producing techniques and his creative process. Louis was promoted to a [http://www.image-line.com/documents/powerusers.php?entry_id=1379898696&title=louis-la-roche-%28brett-ewels%29 FL Studio Power User] in late 2013.\n\nBetween 2011 and 2013 Louis produced a series of 15-minute mixtapes entitled ''''Scenery'''', which have collectively collected over 120,000 plays on [[SoundCloud]]. The press release reads: ''\"Scenery is no ordinary mixtape, all featured songs are edits, remixes, ideas and originals from Louis La Roche. There will be no tracklisting, the idea is that Scenery is a listening experience of short songs that create a journey for the listener. This is a free project, released digitally by myself, and each part will come with individual artwork.\"'' The final instalment of project \u2018'''Scenery Mixtape Part 6 (THE END)'''\u2019 was released on 1 August 2014 and was twice the length of the previous mix tapes.\n\nLouis has shared the stage with artists such as [[Armand Van Helden]], [[A-Trak]], [[Aeroplane (musician)|Aeroplane]], and [[2ManyDJs]]. Since 2008, Louis has toured America, Australia, Brazil, Canada, China, Europe, Indonesia and Malaysia. European countries include: Austria, Belgium, France, Germany, Hungary, Ireland, Italy, The Netherlands, Norway, Poland, Romania, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland and Ukraine. Festival appearances include [[Creamfields]], [[Farmfestival]], [[The Isle of Wight Festival]] and [[Oxygen Festival|Oxygen]].\n\nIn 2014, Louis supported [[Kylie Minogue]] on two dates of her [[Kiss Me Once Tour]].<ref>Arena Riga. http://www.arenariga.com/en/pasakumi/detailed/?events_id=16484  \"Kylie Minogue Kiss Me Once\", [[Arena Riga]] Retrieved on 19 November 2014.</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"2596486":{"pageid":2596486,"ns":0,"title":"Love Inc. He has [[remix]]ed songs by a wide array of performers such as [[Madonna (entertainer)|Madonna]] (\"[[Bedtime Story (Madonna song)|Bedtime Story]]\"), [[t.A.T.u.]] (\"[[All The Things She Said]]\"), [[Paula Abdul]] (\"[[My Love Is for Real]]\"), [[LaTour]] (\"People Are Still Having Sex\"), [[Lisa Stansfield]] (\"[[The Real Thing (Lisa Stansfield song)|The Real Thing]],\" \"[[Never, Never Gonna Give You Up]]\"), [[S Club 7]] (\"[[Two in a Million]]\") and more recently, [[Rihanna]] (\"[[Rockstar 101]]\") and [[Liza Fox]] (\"[[Gimme All (Ring My Bell)]]\"), among many others.\n\nIn the early 2000s, Picchiotti collaborated with pop superstar [[Kylie Minogue]] on two tracks: \"[[Butterfly (Kylie Minogue song)|Butterfly]]\" and \"Give It to Me\". \"Butterfly\" originally appeared on Minogue's 2000 album, ''[[Light Years (Kylie Minogue album)|Light Years]]'', then appeared as a bonus track on her multi-platinum 2002 album, ''[[Fever (Kylie Minogue album)|Fever]]''. Picchiotti produced this track and later remixed it. \"Give It to Me\" appeared on Minogue's ''Fever'' album and was co-written and produced by Picchiotti.\n\nRecently, Picchiotti collaborated with singer-songwriter [[Tom Connan]], remixing his tracks Beautiful Day<ref>http://blog.promotion-us.com/tom-connan-beautiful-day-mark-picchiotti-remixes</ref> and You Didn't Give Them a Chance,<ref>http://dirrtyremixes.tumblr.com/post/77846437867/remixes-tom-connan-you-didnt-give-them</ref> which obtained significant success in the US club circuit.\n\nHe scored his first #1 single on the ''[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]'' [[Hot Dance Club Play]] chart as a featured artist in July 2008, with the song, \"Turn It Up\", which was credited to 'Mark Picchiotti presents Basstoy'. The vocals on \"Turn It Up\" are performed by Dana Devine.  In 2002 he released ''Runnin' '' which reached number 13.<ref>[http://www.musicweek.com/story.asp?storycode=1033692 Picchiotti tops club chart six years after last number one]</ref>"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"843884":{"pageid":843884,"ns":0,"title":"Mark Farina","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{Use mdy dates|date=August 2014}}\n'''Mark Farina''' (born March 25, 1969 in Chicago, Illinois, USA) is a disc jockey and musician, known for his [[Chicago house]], [[acid jazz]] and [[downtempo]] works. Notable releases include ''Mood'' (KMS Records, 1989) and the ''[[Mushroom Jazz]]'' series ([[Om Records]], 1996\u20132011), and recently known also from house compilations ''[[El Divinio]]''. He is primarily identified with the [[house music]] scene in San Francisco, California, where he resides, but DJs widely around the world.\n\nShortly after Mark befriended [[Derrick Carter]] in 1988 at a record store in Chicago, he developed an interest in House music. Mark experimented with a deeper style, dropping De La Soul, disco classics and other styles not being played in the main rooms of nightclubs. While exploring purist forms of House Music, Mark developed his trademark style, known as \"Mushroom Jazz\": acid jazz infused with the West Coast's jazzy, organic productions along with urban beats. Fans embraced Mark's downtempo style, and he started a weekly Mushroom Jazz club night in San Francisco with Patty Ryan. In 3 years at the club, Farina and Mushroom Jazz established a following. When the club closed, Farina continued the tradition by releasing a series of CDs under the same name, ''Mushroom Jazz''. Since then, Mark has been performing hundreds of shows worldwide each year. His House sets have been described as the jazzy side of Chicago House mixed San Francisco style. Some of his sets have been known to last up to 8 hours. Farina has been known to play two different rooms at the same party. URB, MUZIK and BPM Magazines have all had him on their Top DJs in the World lists."}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"4084275":{"pageid":4084275,"ns":0,"title":"Mark Summers","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{About|the record producer|the American television personality|Marc Summers|the Australian rules footballer|Mark Summers (footballer)|the British casting director|Mark Summers (casting director)}}\n{{Multiple issues|\n{{BLP primary sources|date=May 2009}}\n{{advert|date=May 2009}}\n}}\n\n'''Mark Summers''' is the [[CEO]], Sample Replay Producer, [[Sound Engineer]] and [[Music Producer]] of '''Scorccio Sample Replays''', a division of Scorccio Records, a dance music company founded in the UK in 1996.{{Citation needed|date=May 2009}}\n[[File:Mark Summers, CEO of SCORCCiO Sample Replays.jpg|thumb|right|Mark Summers inside the studio at SCORCCiO Sample Replays, February 2012]]"}]}}}}{"query":{"pages":{"909925":{"pageid":909925,"ns":0,"title":"MARRS","revisions":[{"contentformat":"text/x-wiki","contentmodel":"wikitext","*":"{{refimprove|date=August 2008}}\n{{Infobox musical artist <!-- See Wikipedia:WikiProject_Musicians -->\n| name = M{{!}}A{{!}}R{{!}}R{{!}}S\n| image =\n| caption =\n| background = group_or_band\n| origin = [[London, England]]\n| genre = [[House music|House]]\n| years_active = 1987\n| label = [[4AD]] <small>(UK)</small>, [[4th & B'way Records|4th & B\u2019way]]/[[Island Records]] <small>(U.S.)</small>\n| associated_acts = [[A.R.
